form for last will and testament chapter i military discipline and courtesy section 1 oath of enlistment every soldier on enlist in the army take upon himself the follow obligation : i -------- do solemnly swear -lrb- or affirm -rrb- that i will bear true faith and allegiance to the united state of america that i will serve they honestly and faithfully against all they enemy whomsoever and that i will obey the order of the president of the united state and the order of the officer appoint over I accord to the rule and article of war -lrb- 109th article of war -rrb- section 2 obedience the very first paragraph in the army regulation read : all person in the military service be require to obey strictly and to execute promptly the lawful order of they superior obedience be the first and last duty of a soldier it be the foundation upon which all military efficiency be build without it a army become a mob while with it a mob cease to be a mob and become possess of much of the power of a organize force it be a quality that be demand of every person in the army from the highest to the lowest each enlist man bind himself by he enlistment oath to obedience each officer in accept he commission must take upon himself the same solemn obligation obey strictly and execute promptly the lawful order of you superior it be enough to know that the person give the order whether he be a officer a noncommissioned officer or a private act as such be you lawful superior you may not like he you may not respect he but you must respect he position and authority and reflect honor and credit upon yourself and you profession by yield to all superior that complete and unhesitating obedience which be the pleasure as well as the duty of every true soldier order must be strictly carry out it be not sufficient to comply with only that part which suit you or which involve no work or danger or hardship nor be it proper or permissible when you be order to do a thing in a certain way or to accomplish a work in a definitely prescribe manner for you to obtain the same result by other method obedience must be prompt and unquestioning when any soldier -lrb- and this word include officer as well as enlist man -rrb- receive a order it be not for he to consider whether the order be a good one or not whether it would have be better have such a order never be give or whether the duty might be better perform by some one else or at some other time or in some other manner he duty be first to understand just what the order require and second to proceed at once to carry out the order to the best of he ability officer and man of all rank and grade be give a certain independence in the execution of the task to which they be assign and be expect to show initiative in meet the different situation as they arise every individual from the highest commander to the lowest private must always remember that inaction and neglect of opportunity will warrant more severe censure than a error in the choice of the means -lrb- _ preface_field _ _ service_regulations _ -rrb- section 3 loyalty but even with implicit obedience you may yet fail to measure up to that high standard of duty which be at once the pride and glory of every true soldier not until you carry out the desire and wish of you superior in a hearty willing and cheerful manner be you meet all the requirement of you profession for a order be but the will of you superior however it may be express loyalty mean that you be for you organization and its officer and noncommissioned officer -- not against they that you always extend you most earnest and hearty support to those in authority no soldier be a loyal soldier who be a knocker or a grumbler or a shirker just one man of this class in a company breed discontent and dissatisfaction among many other you should therefore not only guard against do such thing yourself but should discourage such action among any of you comrade section 4 discipline 1 all person in the military service be require to obey strictly and to execute promptly the lawful order of they superior 2 military authority will be exercise with firmness kindness and justice punishment must conform to law and follow offens as promptly as circumstance will permit 3 superior be forbid to injure those under they authority by tyrannical or capricious conduct or by abusive language while maintain discipline and the thorough and prompt performance of military duty all officer in deal with enlist man will bear in mind the absolute necessity of so treat they as to preserve they self-respect officer will keep in as close touch as possible with the man under they command and will strive to build up such relation of confidence and sympathy as will insure the free approach of they man to they for counsel and assistance this relationship may be gain and maintain without relaxation of the bond of discipline and with great benefit to the service as a whole 4 courtesy among military man be indispensable to discipline respect to superior will not be confine to obedience on duty but will be extend on all occasion 5 deliberation or discussion among military man convey praise or censure or any mark of approbation toward other in the military service and all publication relate to private or personal transaction between officer be prohibit effort to influence legislation affect the army or to procure personal favor or consideration should never be make except through regular military channel the adoption of any other method by any officer or enlist man will be note in the military record of those concerned -lrb- _ army_regulations _ -rrb- the discipline which make the soldier of a free country reliable in battle be not to be gain by harsh or tyrannical treatment on the contrary such treatment be far more likely to destroy than to make a army it be possible to import instruction and give command in such manner and in such tone of voice as to inspire in the soldier no feeling but a intense desire to obey while the opposite manner and tone of voice can not fall to excite strong resentment and a desire to disobey the one mode or the other of deal with subordinate spring from a corresponding spirit in the breast of the commander he who feel the respect which be due to other can not fail to inspire in they regard for himself while he who feel and hence manifest disrespect toward other especially he inferior can not fail to inspire hatred against himself -lrb- _ address_of_maj_gen_john_m_schofield _ _ to_the_united_states_corps_of_cadets_aug_11_1879 _ -rrb- when by long-continued drill and subordination you have learn you duty and obedience become second nature you have acquire discipline it call not be acquire in a day or a month it be a growth it be the habit of obedience to teach this habit of obedience be the main object of the close-order drill and if good result be to be expect the greatest attention must be pay to even the smallest detail the company or squad must be form promptly at the prescribed time -- not a minute or even a second late all must wear the exact uniform prescribe and in the exact manner prescribe when at attention there must be no gaze about no raising of hand no chewing or spit in rank the manual of arm and all movement must be execute absolutely as prescribe a drill of this kind teach discipline a careless sloppy drill breed disobedience and insubordination in other word discipline simply mean efficiency section 5 military courtesy in all walk of life man who be gentlemanly and of good breeding be always respectful and courteous to those about they it help to make life move along more smoothly in civil life this courtesy be show by the custom of tip the hat to lady shake hand with friend and greet person with a nod or a friendly good morning etc in the army courtesy be just we necessary and for the same reason it help to keep the great machine move without friction courtesy among military man be indispensable to discipline respect to superior will not be confine to obedience on duty but will be extend on all occasion -lrb- _ par_4_army_regulations _ _ 1913 _ -rrb- one method of extend this courtesy be by salute when in rank the question of what a private should do be simple -- he obey any command that be give it be when out of rank that a private must know how and when to salute section 6 salute in the old day the free man of europe be all allow to carry weapon and when they meet each would hold up he right hand to show that he have no weapon in it and that they meet as friend slave or serf however be not allow to carry weapon and slink past the free man without make any sign in this way the salute come to be the symbol or sign by which soldier -lrb- free man -rrb- might recognize each other the lower class begin to imitate the soldier in this respect although in a clumsy apologetic way and thence creep into civil life the custom of raise the hand or nodding as one pass a acquaintance the soldier however keep they individual salute and purposely make it intricate and difficult to learn in order that it could be acquire only by the constant training all real soldier receive to this day army have preserve they salute and when correctly do it be at once recognize and never mistake for that of the civilian all soldier should be careful to execute the salute exactly as prescribe the civilian or the imitation soldier who try to imitate the military salute invariably make some mistake which show that he be not a real soldier he give it in a apologetic manner he fail to stand or march at attention he coat be unbuttoned or hat on awry or he fall to look the person salute in the eye there be a wide difference in the method of render and mean between the civilian salute as use by friend in pass or by servant to they employer and the military salute the symbol and sign of the military profession to salute with the hand first assume the position of a soldier or march at attention look the officer you be to salute straight in the eye then when the proper distance separate you raise the right hand smartly till the tip of the forefinger touch the lower part of the headdress or forehead above the right eye thumb and finger extend and join palm to the left forearm incline at about 45 ° hand and wrist straight continue to look the officer you be salute straight in the eye and keep you hand in the position of salute until the officer acknowledge the salute or until he have pass then drop the hand smartly to the side the salute be give with the right hand only to salute with the rifle bring the rifle to right shoulder arm if not already there carry the left hand smartly to the small of the stock forearm horizontal palm of the hand down thumb and finger extend and join forefinger touch the end of the cock piece look the officer salute in the eye when the officer have acknowledge the salute or have pass drop the left hand smartly to the side and turn the head and eye to the front the rifle salute may also be execute from the order or trail see paragraph 94 infantry drill regulation and paragraph 111 cavalry drill regulation 1916 to salute with the saber bring the saber to order saber if not already there raise and carry the saber to the front base of the hilt as high as the chin and 6 inch in front of the neck edge to the left point 6 inch farther to the front than the hilt thumb extend on the left of the grip all finger grasp the grip look the officer salute in the eye when the officer have acknowledge the salute or have pass lower the saber point in prolongation of the right foot and near the ground edge to the left hand by the side thumb on left of grip arm extend and return to the order saber if mount the hand be hold behind the thigh point a little to the right and front of the stirrup -lrb- for cavalry -rrb- to salute with the saber bring the saber to carry saber if not already there carry the saber to the front with arm half extend until the thumb be about 6 inch in front of the chin the blade vertical guard to the leave all four finger grasp the grip the thumb extend along the back in the groove the finger press the back of the grip against the heel of the hand look the officer salute in the eye when the officer have acknowledge the salute or have pass bring the saber down with the blade against the hollow of the right shoulder guard to the front right hand at the hip the third and fourth finger on the back of the grip and the elbow back the pistol be not carry in the hand but in the holster therefore when arm with the pistol salute with the hand always stand or march at attention before and during the salute the hat should be on straight coat completely button up and hand out of the pocket section 7 rule govern salute 759 -lrb- 1 -rrb- salute shall be exchange between officer and enlist man not in a military formation nor at drill work game or mess on every occasion of they meeting pass near or be address the officer junior in rank or the enlist man salute first -lrb- 2 -rrb- when a officer enter a room where there be several enlist man the word attention be give by some one who perceive he when all rise uncover and remain standing at attention until the officer leave the room or direct otherwise enlist man at meal stop eat and remain seat at attention -lrb- 3 -rrb- a enlist man if seat rise on the approach of a officer face toward he stand at attention and salute stand he face a officer for the same purpose if the party remain in the same place or on the same ground such compliment need not be repeat soldier actually at work do not cease work to salute a officer unless address by he -lrb- 4 -rrb- before address a officer a enlist man make the prescribe salute with the weapon with which he be armed or if unarmed with the right hand he also make the same salute after receive a reply -lrb- 5 -rrb- in uniform covered or uncovered but not in formation officer and enlist man salute military person as follow : with arm in hand the salute prescribe for that arm -lrb- sentinel on interior guard duty except -rrb- without arm the right-hand salute -lrb- 6 -rrb- in civilian dress cover or uncovered officer and enlist man salute military person with the right-hand salute -lrb- 7 -rrb- officer and enlist man will render the prescribe salute in a military manner the officer junior in rank or the enlist man salute first when several officer in company be salute all entitle to the salute shall return it -lrb- 8 -rrb- except in the field under campaign or simulated campaign condition a mount officer -lrb- or soldier -rrb- dismount before address a superior officer not mount -lrb- 9 -rrb- a man in formation shall not salute when directly address but shall come to attention if at rest or at ease -lrb- 10 -rrb- salute distance be that within which recognition be easy in general it do not exceed 30 pace -lrb- 11 -rrb- when a officer entitle to the salute pass in rear of a body of troops it be bring to attention while he be opposite the post of the commander -lrb- 12 -rrb- in public conveyance such as railway train and street car and in public place such as theater honor and personal salute may be omit when palpably inappropriate or apt to disturb or annoy civilian present -lrb- 13 -rrb- soldier at all time and in all situation pay the same compliment to officer of the army navy marine corps and volunteer and to officer of the national guard as to officer of they own regiment corps or arm of service -lrb- 14 -rrb- sentinel on post do interior guard duty conform to the foregoing principle but salute by present arm when arm with the rifle they will not salute if it interfere with the proper performance of they duty troops under arm will salute we prescribe in drill regulation 760 -lrb- 1 -rrb- commander of detachment or other command will salute officer of grade higher than the person command the unit by first bring the unit to attention and then salute as require by subparagraph -lrb- 5 -rrb- paragraph 759 if the person salute be of a junior or equal grade the unit need not be at attention in the exchange of salute -lrb- 2 -rrb- if two detachment or other command meet they commander will exchange salute both command be at attention 761 salute and honor as a rule be not pay by troops actually engage in drill on the march or in the field under campaign or simulated campaign condition troops on the service of security pay no compliment whatever 762 if the command be in line at a halt -lrb- not in the field -rrb- and arm with the rifle or with saber draw it shall be bring to present arm or present saber before its commander salute in the follow case : when the national anthem be play or when to the color or to the standard be sound during ceremony or when a person be salute who be its immediate or higher commander or a general officer or when the national or regimental color be salute 763 at parade and other ceremony under arm the command shall render the prescribe salute and shall remain in the position of salute while the national anthem be be play also at retreat and during ceremony when to the color be play if no band be present if not under arm the organization shall be bring to attention at the first note of the national anthem to the color or to the standard and the salute render by the officer or noncommissioned officer in command as prescribe in regulation as amend herein 764 whenever the national anthem be play at any place when person belong to the military service be present all officer and enlist man not in formation shall stand at attention face toward the music -lrb- except at retreat when they shall face toward the flag -rrb- if in uniform covered or uncovered or in civilian clothes uncover they shall salute at the first note of the anthem retain the position of salute until the last note of the anthem if not in uniform and cover they shall uncover at the first note of the anthem hold the headdress opposite the left shoulder and so remain until its close except that in inclement weather the headdress may be slightly raise the same rule apply when to the color or to the standard be sound as when the national anthem be play when play by a army band the national anthem shall be play through without repetition of any part not require to be repeat to make it complete the same mark of respect prescribe for observance during the playing of the national anthem of the united state shall be show toward the national anthem of any other country when play upon official occasion 765 officer and enlist man pass the uncased color will render honor as follow : if in uniform they will salute as require by subparagraph -lrb- 5 -rrb- paragraph 759 if in civilian dress and cover they will uncover hold the headdress opposite the left shoulder with the right hand if uncover they will salute with the right-hand salute -lrb- _ infantry_drill_regulations _ _ 1911 _ -rrb- the national flag belong to dismount organization be call a color to mount organization a standard a uncased color be one that be not in its waterproof cover private do not salute noncommissioned officer prisoner be not permit to salute they merely come to attention if not actually at work the playing of the national anthem as a part of a medley be prohibit in the military service section 8 courtesy in conversation in speak to a officer always stand at attention and use the word sir example : sir private brown company b report as orderly sir the first sergeant direct I to report to the captain -lrb- question by a officer : -rrb- to what company do you belong -lrb- answer : -rrb- company h sir -lrb- question by a officer : -rrb- have first call for drill sound -lrb- answer : -rrb- no sir or yes sir it sound about five minute ago -lrb- question by a officer : -rrb- can you tell I please where major smith 's tent be -lrb- answer : -rrb- yes sir i 'll take you to it use the third person in speak to a officer example : do the lieutenant wish etc do the captain send for I in deliver a message from one officer to another always use the form similar to the following : lieutenant a present he compliment to captain b and state etc this form be not use when the person send or receive the message be a enlist man in all official conversation refer to other soldier by they title thus : sergeant b private c -lrb- illustration -rrb- chapter ii arm uniform and equipment section 1 the rifle the rifle now use by the army of the united state be the united state magazine rifle model of 1903 caliber 30 it be 43212 inch long and weigh 869 pound the bayonet weigh 1 pound and the blade be 16 inch long the rifle be sight for range up to 2850 yard the maximum range when elevated at a angle of 45 degree be 4891 yard -lrb- 389 yard less than 3 mile -rrb- the smooth bear of the rifle be 030 inch in diameter it be then rifle 0004 inch deep make the diameter from the bottom of one groove to the bottom of the opposite groove 0308 inch the rifle make one complete turn in each 10 inch of the barrel the accompany plate show the name of the principal part of the rifle the only part of a rifle that a enlist man be permit to take apart be the bolt mechanism and the magazine mechanism learn how to do this from you squad leader for you must know how in order to keep you rifle clean never remove the hand guard or the trigger guard nor take the sight apart unless you have special permission from a commission officer the cartridge use for the rifle be call the 30-caliber model 1906 cartridge there be four type of cartridge the ball cartridge consist of the brass case or shell the primer the charge of smokeless powder and the bullet the bullet have a sharp point be compose of a lead core and a jacket of cupro nickel and weigh 150 grain the bullet of this cartridge when fire from the rifle start with a initial velocity at the muzzle of 2700 foot per second the blank cartridge contain a paper cup instead of a bullet it be dangerous up to 100 foot firing with blank cartridge at a represent enemy at range less than 100 yard be prohibit the guard cartridge have a smaller charge of powder than the ball cartridge and five cannelure encircle the body of the shell at about the middle to distinguish it from the ball cartridge it be intend for use on guard or in riot duty and give good result up to 200 yard the range of 100 yard require a sight elevation of 450 yard and the range of 200 yard require all elevation of 650 yard the dummy cartridge be tin plate and the shell be provide with six longitudinal corrugation and three circular hole the primer contain no percussion composition it be intend for drill purpose to accustom the soldier to the operation of load the rifle all cartridge be secure five in a clip to enable five cartridge to be insert into the magazine at one motion sixty ball cartridge in 12 clip be pack in a cloth bandoleer to facilitate issue and carry when full the bandoleer weigh about 388 pound bandoleer be packed 20 in a box or 1200 round in all the full box weigh 99 pound section 2 care of the rifle every part of the rifle must be keep free from rust dust and dirt a dirty or rusty rifle be a sure sign that the soldier do not realize the value of he weapon and that he training be incomplete the rifle you be arm with be the most accurate in the world if it get dirty or rusty it will deteriorate in its accuracy and work efficiency and no subsequent care will restore it to its original condition the most important part of the rifle to keep clean be the bear if after firing the bear be leave dirty over night it will be badly rust in the morning therefore you rifle must be clean not later than the evening of the day on which it be fire the fouling of the blank cartridge be as dangerous to the bear as the fouling of the ball cartridge never attempt to polish any part that be blue if rust appear remove by rub with oil never use emery paper pomade or any preparation that cut or scratch to clean any part of the rifle to beautify and preserve the stock rub with raw linseed oil the use of any other preparation on the stock be strictly forbid always handle you rifle with care do not throw it around as though it be a club do not stand it up against anything so that it rest against the front sight do not leave a stopper or a rag in the bear : it will cause rust to form at that point it may also cause the gun barrel to burst if a shot be fire before remove it guard the sight and muzzle carefully from any blow that might injure they the front sight cover should always be on the rifle except when rifle be be fire this be especially necessary to protect the front sight while rifle be be carry in scabbard by a mount man in come to the order arm lower the piece gently to the ground when there be a cartridge in the chamber the piece be always carry lock in this position the safety lock should be keep turn fully to the right since if it be turn to the left nearly to the ready position and the trigger be pull the rifle will be discharge when the safety lock be turn to the ready position at any time later on cartridge can not be load from the magazine unless the bolt be draw fully to the rear when the bolt be close or only partly open the cut-off may be turn up or down as desire but if the bolt be draw fully to the rear the magazine can not be cut off unless the top cartridge or the follower be press down slightly and the bolt be push forward so that the cut-off may be turn off in the case of a misfire do not open the bolt immediately as it may be a hangfire misfire be often due to the fact that the bolt handle be not fully press down sometimes in pull the trigger the soldier raise the bolt handle without know it unless otherwise order arm will be unloaded before be take to quarter or tent or as soon as the man use they be relieve from duty keep the work part oil in every company there should be at least one copy of the manual of the ordnance department entitle description and rule for the management of the u s magazine rifle this manual give the name and a cut of every part of the rifle explain its use show how to take the rifle apart and care for the same and also give much other valuable and interesting information section 3 cleaning the rifle clean the rifle -- -lrb- a -rrb- the proper care of the bear require conscientious careful work but it pay well in the attainment of reduce labor of clean prolonged accuracy life of the barrel and better result in target practice briefly state the care of the bear consist in remove the foul result from firing to obtain a chemically clean surface and in coating this surface with a film of oil to prevent rusting the fouling which result from firing be of two kind -- one the product of combustion of the powder the other cupro-nickel scrape off -lrb- under the abrade action of irregularity or grit in the bear -rrb- powder fouling because of its acid reaction be highly corrosive that be it will induce rust and must be remove metal fouling of itself be inactive but may cover powder fouling and prevent the action of clean agent until remove and when accumulate in noticeable quantity it reduce the accuracy of the rifle -lrb- b -rrb- powder fouling may be readily remove by scrub with hot soda solution but this solution have no effect on the metal fouling of cupro-nickel it be necessary therefore to remove all metal fouling before assurance can be have that all powder fouling have be remove and that the bear may be safely oil normally after firing a barrel in good condition the metal fouling be so slight as to be hardly perceptible it be merely a smear of infinitesimal thickness easily remove by solvent of cupro-nickel however due to pit the presence of dust other abrasive or to accumulation metal fouling may occur in clearly visible flake or patch of much greater thickness much more difficult to remove -lrb- c -rrb- in clean the bear after firing it be well to proceed as follow : swab out the bear with soda solution -lrb- subparagraph j -rrb- to remove powder foul a convenient method be to insert the muzzle of the rifle into the can contain the soda solution and with the cleaning rod insert from the breech pump the barrel full a few time remove and dry with a couple of patch examine the bear to see that there be in evidence no patch of metal fouling which if present can be readily detect by the naked eye then swab out with the swab solution -- a dilute metal-fouling solution -lrb- subparagraph j -rrb- the amount of swab require with the swab solution can be determine only by experience assist by the color of the patch swab should be continue however as long as the wipe patch be discolor by a bluish-green stain normally a couple of minute ' work be sufficient dry thoroughly and oil -lrb- d -rrb- the proper method of oil a barrel be as follow : wipe the cleaning roll dry select a clean patch and thoroughly saturate it with sperm oil or warm cosmic be sure that the cosmic have penetrate the patch scrub the bear with the patch finally draw the patch smoothly from the muzzle to the breech allow the cleaning rod to turn with the rifle the bear will be find now to be smooth and bright so that any subsequent rust and sweating can be easily detect by inspection -lrb- e -rrb- if patch of metal fouling be see upon visual inspection of the bear the standard metal foul solution prepare as hereinafter prescribe must be use after scrub out with the soda solution plug the bear from the breech with a cork at the front end of the chamber or where the rifle begin slip a 2-inch section of rubber hose over the muzzle down to the sight and fill with the standard solution to at least one-half inch above the muzzle of the barrel let it stand for 30 minute pour out the standard solution remove hose and breech plug and swab out thoroughly with soda solution to neutralize and remove all trace of ammonia and powder fouling wipe the barrel clean dry and oil with few exception one application be sufficient but if all fouling be not remove as determine by careful visual inspection of the bear and of the wipe patch repeat as describe above -lrb- f -rrb- after properly clean with either the swab solution or the standard solution as have just be describe the bear should be clean and safe to oil and put away but as a measure of safety a patch should always be run through the bear on the next day and the bear and wipe patch examine to insure that cleaning have be properly accomplish the bear should then be oil as describe above -lrb- g -rrb- if the swab solution or the standard metal-fouling solution be not available the barrel should be scrub as already describe with the soda solution dry and oil with a light oil at the end of 24 hour it should again be clean when it will usually be find to have sweat that be rust have form under the smear of metal foul where powder fouling be present the surface be puff up usually a second cleaning be sufficient but to insure safety it should be again examine at the end of a few day before final oil the swab solution should always be use if available for it must be remember that each puff when the bear sweat be a incipient rust pit -lrb- h -rrb- a clean dry surface have be obtain to prevent rust it be necessary to coat every portion of this surface with a film of neutral oil if the protection require be but temporary and the arm be to be clean or fire in a few day sperm oil may be use this be easily apply and easily remove but have not sufficient body to hold its surface for more than a few day if rifle be to be prepare for storage or shipment a heavier oil such as cosmic must be use -lrb- i -rrb- in prepare arm for storage or shipment they should be clean with particular care use the metal-fouling solution as describe above care should be take insure by careful inspection on succeed day or day that the cleaning be properly do and all trace of ammonia solution remove the bear be then ready to be coat with cosmic at ordinary temperature cosmic be not fluid in order therefore to insure that every part of the surface be coat with a film of oil the cosmic should be warm apply the cosmic first with a brush then with the breech plug fill the barrel to the muzzle pour out the surplus remove the breechblock and allow to drain it be believe that more rifle be ruin by improper preparation for storage than from any other cause if the bear be not clean when oil -- that be if powder fouling be present or rust have start -- a half inch of cosmic on the outside will not stop its action and the barrel will be ruin remember that the surface must be perfectly clean before the heavy oil be apply if the instruction as give above be carefully follow arm may be store for year without harm -lrb- j -rrb- preparation of solution : _ soda_solution _ -- this should be a saturated solution or sal soda -lrb- bicarbonate of soda -rrb- a strength of at least 20 per cent be necessary the spoon refer to in the follow direction be the model 1910 spoon issue in the mess outfit sal soda one-fourth pound or four -lrb- 4 -rrb- heap spoonful water 1 pint or cup model of 1910 to upper rivet the sal soda will dissolve more readily in hot water _ swabbing_solution _ -- ammonium persulphate 60 grain one-half spoonful smooth off ammonia 28 per cent 6 ounce or three-eighth of a pint or 12 spoonful water 4 ounce or one-fourth pint or 8 spoonful dissolve the ammonium persulphate in the water and add the ammonia keep in tightly cork bottle pour out only what be necessary at the time and keep the bottle corked _ standard_metal_fouling_solution _ -- ammonium persulphate 1 ounce or 2 medium heaping spoonful ammonium carbonate 200 grain or 1 heaping spoonful ammonia 28 per cent 6 ounce or three-eighths pint or 12 spoonful water 4 ounce or one-fourth pint or 8 spoonful powder the persulphate and carbonate together dissolve in the water and add the ammonia mix thoroughly and allow to stand for one hour before use it should be keep in a strong bottle tightly cork the solution should not be use more than twice and use solution should not be mix with unused solution but should be bottled separately the solution when mix should be use within 30 day care should be exercise in mix and use this solution to prevent injury to the rifle a experienced noncommissioned officer should mix the solution and superintend its use neither of these ammonia solution have any appreciable action on steel when not expose to the air but if allow to evaporate on steel they attack it rapidly care should therefore be take that none spill on the mechanism and that the barrel be wash out promptly with soda solution the first application of soda solution remove the greater portion of the powder fouling and permit a more effective and economical use of the ammonia solution these ammonia solution be expensive and should be use economically -lrb- k -rrb- it be a fact recognize by all that a highly polish steel surface rust much less easily than one which be roughen : also that a barrel which be pit foul much more rapidly than one which be smooth every effort therefore should be make to prevent the formation of pit which be merely enlarged rust spot and which not only affect the accuracy of the arm but increase the labor of cleaning -lrb- l -rrb- the chamber of rifle be frequently neglect because they be not readily inspect care should be take to see that they be clean as thoroughly as the bear a roughened chamber delay greatly the rapidity of fire and not infrequently cause shell to stick -lrb- m -rrb- a cleaning rack should be provide for every barrack rifle should always be clean from the breach thus avoid possible injury to the rifle at the muzzle which would affect the shooting adversely if the bear for a length of 6 inch at the muzzle be perfect a minor injury near the chamber will have little effect on the accuracy of the rifle the rifle should be clean as soon as the firing for the day be complete the fouling be easier to remove then and if left longer it will corrode the barrel -lrb- n -rrb- the principle as outline above apply equally well for the care of the barrel of the automatic pistol special attention should be pay to clean the chamber of the pistol use the soda solution it have be find that the chamber pit readily if it be not carefully clean with the result that the operation of the pistol be make less certain -lrb- _ par_134_small_arms _ _ firing_manual_1913 _ -rrb- section 4 uniform uniform and clothing issue to enlist man must not be sell pawned loan give away lose or damage through neglect or carelessness any soldier who violate this rule may be try by a military court and punish all uniform and article of clothing issue to enlist man whether or not charge on they clothing allowance remain the property of the united state and do not become the property of the soldier either before or after discharge from the service under the law a soldier honorably discharge from the army of the united state be authorize to wear he uniform from the place of he discharge to he home within three month after the date of such discharge to wear the uniform after three month from the date of such discharge render such person liable to fine or imprisonment or both the dress uniform -lrb- the blue uniform -rrb- consist of the show above the collar of the coat turndown piccadilly or roll collar be not authorize when under arm white glove and the garrison belt -lrb- or russet-leather belt and cartridge box -rrb- be wear the uniform never wear any part of the uniform with civilian clothes it be very unsoldierly for example to wear a civilian overcoat over the uniform or to wear the uniform overcoat over a civilian suit should be promptly replace there be but one correct and soldierly way to wear the cap never wear it on the back or side of the head the service hat should be worn in the regulation shape peak with four indentation and with hat cord sew on do not cover it with pen or pencil mark never appear outside you room or tent with you coat or olive-drab shirt unbuttoned or collar of coat unhooked chevron chapter iii ration and forage section 1 the ration a ration be the allowance of food for one man for one day in the field there be three kind of ration issue as follow : the _ garrison_ration _ be intend to be issue in kind whenever possible the approximate net weight of this ration be 45 pound the _ reserve_ration _ be the simplest efficient ration and constitute the reserve carry for field service it consist of -- ounce bacon 12 hard bread 16 coffee roasted and ground 112 sugar 24 salt 16 ----- approximate net weight pound 2 the _ field_ration _ be the ration prescribe in order by the commander of the field force it consist of the reserve ration in whole or in part supplement by article requisition or purchase locally or ship from the rear in campaign a command carry as a part of its normal equipment the follow ration : -lrb- a -rrb- on each man : at least two day ' reserve ration -lrb- b -rrb- in the ration section of the field train for each man : two day ' field and one day 's reserve ration -lrb- c -rrb- in the supply train : two day ' field ration in addition to the foregoing commander will require each man on the march to carry the unconsumed portion of the day 's ration issue the night before for the noonday meal reserve ration be consume only in case of extreme necessity when other supplies be not available they be not to be consume or renew without a express order from the officer in command of the troops who be responsible for the provision of supplies namely the division commander or other independent-detachment commander every officer within the limit of he command be hold responsible for the enforcement of this regulation reserve ration consume must he replace at the first opportunity section 2 individual cooking sometimes ration for several day be issue to the soldier at one time and in such case you should be very careful to so use the ration that they will last you the entire period if you stuff yourself one day or waste you ration you will have to starve later on generally the cooking for the company will be do by the company cook but sometimes every soldier will have to prepare he own meal use only he field mess kit for the purpose the best fire for individual cooking be a small clear one or better yet a few brisk coal to make such a fire first gather a number of stick about 1 inch in diameter these should be dry dead limb adhering to a tree be dryer than those pick up from the ground split some of these and shave they up into kindle dig a trench in the ground lay with the wind about a foot long 4 inch wide and 6 inch deep start the fire in this trench gradually pile on the heavier wood as the fire grow when the trench be full of burn wood allow it a few minute to burn down to the coal and stop blaze high then rest the meat can and cup over the trench and start cooking either may be support if necessary with green stick if you can not scrape a trench in the soil build one up out of rock or with two parallel log the following recipe have be furnish from the office of the quartermaster general united state army : _ coffee _ -- fill the cup two-third full of water and bring to a boil add one heap spoonful of coffee and stir well add one spoonful of sugar if desire boil five minute and then set it to the side of the fire to simmer for about 10 minute then to clear the coffee throw in a spoonful or two of cold water this coffee be of medium strength and be within the limit of the ration if make but twice a day _ cocoa _ -- take two-third of a cupful of water bring to a boil add one heap spoonful of cocoa and stir until dissolve add one spoonful of sugar if desire and boil for five minute _ chocolate _ -- take two-third of a cupful of water bring to a boil add a piece of chocolate about the size of a hickory nut breaking or cut it into small piece and stir until dissolve add one spoonful of sugar if desire and boil for five minute _ tea _ -- take two-third of a cupful of water bring to a boll add one-half of a level spoonful of tea and then let it stand or draw for three minute if allow to stand longer the tea will get bitter unless separate from the ten leave meat _ bacon _ -- cut slice about five to the inch three of which should generally be sufficient for one man for one meal place in a meat can with about one-half inch of cold water let come to a boll and then pour the water off fry over a brisk fire turn the bacon once and quickly brown it remove the bacon to lid of meat can leave the grease for fry potato onion rice flapjack etc accord to recipe _ fresh_meat _ -lrb- to fry -rrb- -- to fry a small amount of grease -lrb- one to two spoonful -rrb- be necessary put grease in the meat can and let come to a smoking temperature then drop in the steak and if about one-half inch thick let fry for about one minute before turn depend upon whether it be desire it shall be rare medium or well do then turn and fry briskly as before salt and pepper to taste apply to beef veal pork mutton venison etc _ fresh_meat _ -lrb- to broil -rrb- -- cut in slice about one inch thick from half as large as the hand to four time that size sharpen a stick or branch of convenient length -- say from two to four foot long -- and weave the point of the stick through the steak several time so that it may be readily turn over a few brisk coal or on the windward side of a small fire allow to brown nicely turn frequently salt and pepper to taste meat with considerable fat be prefer though any meat may be broil in this manner _ fresh_meat _ -lrb- to stew -rrb- -- cut into chunk from one-half inch to one inch cube fill cup about one-third full of meat and cover with about one inch of water let boil or simmer about one hour or until tender add such fibrous vegetable as carrot turnip or cabbage cut into small chunk soon after the meat be put on to boil and potato onion or other tender vegetable when the meat be about half do amount of vegetable to be add about the same as meat depend upon supply and taste salt and pepper to taste apply to ail fresh meat and fowl the proportion of meat and vegetable use vary with they abundance and fix quantity can not be adhere to fresh fish can be handle as above except that it be cook much quicker and potato and onion and can corn be the only vegetable generally use with it thus make a chowder a slice of bacon would greatly improve the flavor may be conveniently cook in meat can or cup vegetable _ potato _ -lrb- fry -rrb- -- take two medium-sized potato or one large one -lrb- about one-half pound -rrb- peel and cut into slice about one-fourth inch thick and scatter well in the meat can in which the grease remain after try the bacon add sufficient water to half cover the potato cover with the lid to keep the moisture in and let come to a boil for about 15 to 20 minute remove the cover and dry as desire salt and pepper to taste during the cooking the bacon already prepare may be keep on the cover which be most conveniently place bottom side up over the cooking vegetable _ onion _ -lrb- fry -rrb- -- same as potato _ potato _ -lrb- boil -rrb- -- peel two medium-sized potato -lrb- about one-half pound -rrb- or one large one and cut in coarse chunk of about the same size -- say 1-1\/2 inch cube place in meat can and three-fourths fill with water cover with lid and let boil or simmer for 15 or 20 minute they be do when easily penetrate with a sharp stick pour off the water and let dry out for one or two minute over hot ash or light coal _ potato _ -lrb- baked -rrb- -- take two medium-sized potato -lrb- about one-half pound -rrb- or one large one cut in half lay in a bed of light coal and cover with same and smother with ash do not disturb for 30 or 40 minute when they should be do _ canned_tomatoes _ -- one 2-pound can be generally sufficient for five man _ stew _ -- pour into the meat can one man 's allowance of tomato and add about two large hardtack break into small piece and let come to a boil add salt and pepper to taste or add a pinch of salt and one-fourth spoonful of sugar _ or _ have try the bacon pour the tomato into the meat can the grease remain and add if desire two broken hardtack set over a brisk fire and let come to a boil _ or _ heat the tomato just as they come from the can add two pinch of salt and one-half spoonful of sugar if desire _ or _ especially in hot weather eat cold with hard bread they be very palatable _ rice _ -- take about two-third of a cupful of water bring to a boll add four heap spoonful of rice and boil until the grain be soft enough to be easily mash between the finger -lrb- about 20 minute -rrb- add two pinch of salt and after stir pour off the water and empty rice out on meat can bacon grease or sugar may be add _ corn_meal_fine_hominy_oatmeal _ -- take about one-third of a cupful of water bring to a boil add 4 heap spoonful of the meal or hominy and boil about 20 minute then add about two pinch of salt and stir well _ dried_beans_and_peas _ -- put 4 heaping spoonful in about two-third of a cupful of water and boil until soft this generally take from three to four hour add one pinch of salt about half a hour before the bean be do add one slice of bacon hot bread _ flapjack _ -- take 6 spoonful of flour and one-third spoonful of bake powder and mix thoroughly -lrb- or dry mix in a large pan before issue at the rate of 25 pound of flour and 3 half can of bake powder for 100 man -rrb- add sufficient cold water to make a batter that will drip freely from the spoon add a pinch of salt pour into the meat can which should contain the grease from fried bacon or a spoonful of butter or fat and place over medium hot coal sufficient to bake so that in from 5 to 7 minute the flapjack may be turn by a quick toss of the pan fry from 5 to 7 minute longer or until by examination it be find to be do _ hoecake _ -- hoecake be make exactly the same as flapjack by substitute _ corn_meal _ for _ flour _ _ emergency_rations _ -- detailed instruction as to the manner of prepare the emergency ration be find on the label of each can remember that even a very limited amount of bacon or hard bread or both consume with the emergency ration make it far more palatable and generally extend the period during which it can be consume with relish for this reason it would be better to husband the supply of hard bread and bacon for use with the emergency ration when it become evident that the latter must be consume rather than to retain the emergency ration to the last extremity and force its exclusive use for a longer period than two or three day section 3 the forage ration _ 1077_army_regulations _ -- the forage ration for a horse be 14 pound of hay and 12 pound of oats corn or barley and 3-1\/3 pound of straw -lrb- or hay -rrb- for bedding for a field artillery horse of the heavy-draft type weigh 1300 pound or over 17 pound of hay and 14 pound of oats corn or barley and 3-1\/3 pound of straw -lrb- or hay -rrb- for bedding for a mule 14 pound of hay and 9 pound of oats corn or barley and 3-1\/3 pound of straw -lrb- or hay -rrb- for bedding to each animal 3 pound of bran may be issue in lieu of that quantity of grain the commanding officer may in he discretion vary the proportion of the component of the ration -lrb- 1 pound of grain 1-1\/2 pound of hay and 2 pound of straw be take as equivalent -rrb- and in the field may substitute other recognize article of forage obtain locally the variation or the substitution not to exceed the money value of the component of the ration at the contract rate in effect at the time of change _ 1078_army_regulations _ -- where grazing be practicable or when little work be require of the animal command officer will reduce the forage ration when on the other hand condition demand it they be authorize to increase the ration not in excess however of savings make in the field the authorize allowance must often be reduce and supplement by grazing and other kind of food such as green forage bean pea rice palay wheat and rye wheat and rye should be crush and feed sparingly -lrb- about one-fourth of the allowance -rrb- for unshelled corn add about one-quarter weight on the march the grain ration be the only forage carry it consist of 12 pound of grain for each horse and 9 pound of grain for each mule recourse must be have to grazing if it be not possible to procure long forage in the country traverse in campaign a command carry as a part of its normal equipment the follow forage : -lrb- a -rrb- for each draft animal : on each vehicle a _ reserve _ of one day 's grain ration for its draft animal -lrb- b -rrb- on animal and vehicle : a portion of they grain ration issue the night before for a noonday feed -lrb- c -rrb- in the ration section of the field train for each animal two day 's grain ration -lrb- d -rrb- in supply train of a infantry division two day ' grain ration and of a cavalry division one day ' grain ration chapter iv personal hygiene and care of the foot personal hygiene history show that in almost every war many more man die of disease than from wound receive in battle much of this disease be preventable and be due either to the ignorance or carelessness of the person who have the disease or of other person about he it be a terrible truth that one man who violate any of the great rule of health may be the means of kill many more of he comrade than be kill by the bullet of the enemy it be therefore most important that every soldier should learn how to take care of he health when in the field and that he should also insist that he comrade do not violate any of the rule prescribe for this purpose a great many disease be due to germ which be either little animal or little plant so very small that they can only be see by aid of the microscope all disease cause by germ be catch all other disease be not catch there be only five way of catch disease : -lrb- a -rrb- get certain germ on the body by touch some one or something which have they on it thus one may catch venereal disease smallpox measles scarlet fever chicken pox mumps boll body louse ringworm barber 's itch dhopie itch and some other disease wound be infect in this manner -lrb- b -rrb- breathing in certain germ which float in the air in this way one may catch pneumonia consumption influenza diphtheria whooping cough tonsilitis spinal meningitis measles and certain other disease -lrb- c -rrb- take certain germ in through the mouth in eating or drinking dysentery cholera typhoid fever diarrhea and intestinal worm may be catch in this manner -lrb- d -rrb- have certain germ inject into the body by the bite of insect such as mosquito flea and bedbug malaria yellow fever dengue fever and bubonic plague may be catch in this way -lrb- e -rrb- inherit the germ from one 's parent person may have these germ sometimes without apparently be sick with any disease such person and person who be sick with the disease be a great source of danger to other about they germ which multiply in such person be find in they urine and excretion from the bowels in discharge from ulcer and abscess in the spit or particle cough or sneeze into the air in the perspiration or scale from the skin and in the blood suck up by bite insect those who have take care of they health and who have not become weaken by bad habit exposure and fatigue be not only less liable to catch disease but be more apt to recover when take sick know all these thing the soldier can understand the reason for the follow rule and how important it be that they should be carry out by each and every person : stay away from person have catch disease it you have any disease do not try to cure it yourself but go to the surgeon insist that other soldier do likewise typhoid fever be one of the most dangerous and common camp disease modern medicine have however discover a effective preventative for this disease in the typhoid prophylactic which render the person immune from typhoid fever the treatment consist in inject into the arm a preventative serum the injection be give three time at 10-day interval association with lewd woman be dangerous it may result in disable you for life it be the cause of a disease -lrb- syphilis -rrb- which may be transmit by a parent to he child soldier with venereal disease should not use basin or toilet article use by other as the germ of these disease if get into the eye very often cause blindness likewise if they use the same drinking cup use by other they may give other the disease they should promptly report they trouble to the surgeon that they may receive the best medical advice and attention should a soldier expose himself to infection by have intercourse with a unknown woman he should report as soon as possible afterwards to the regimental infirmary for prophylactic treatment which if take within a few hour after intercourse will prevent to a large degree the liability of contract any disease cook germ be dead and therefore harmless water even when clear may be alive with deadly germ therefore when the condition be such that the commanding officer order all drinking water to be boil be careful to live up to this order use the latrine and do not go elsewhere to relieve yourself in open latrine cover you deposit with dirt as it breed file and may also be full of germ fly carry germ from one place to another therefore see that you food and mess kit be protect from they all slop find scrap of food scatter about camp soon produce bad odor and draw fly therefore do you part toward keep the camp free from disease by carefully deposit such refuse in the pit or can use for this purpose urinate only in the latrine or in the can set out for this purpose never on the ground around camp because it not only cause bad smell but urine sometimes contain the germ of catch disease soapy water throw on the ground soon produce bad odor therefore in camp of several day ' duration this water should be throw in covered pit or in can use for this purpose as certain mosquito can transmit malaria and yellow fever use you mosquito bar for this reason as well as for personal comfort keep you mouth clean by brushing you tooth once or twice a day it help to prevent the tooth from decay decayed tooth cause toothache they also lead one to swallow food without properly chew it and this lead to stomach trouble of various kind food leave around and between the tooth be bad for the tooth and form good breed place for germ keep the skin clean through the pore of the skin the body get rid of much waste and poisonous matter therefore remove this and keep the pore open by bathing once every day if possible if water be scarce rub the body over with a wet towel if no water be at hand take a dry rub wash carefully the armpit between the leg and under the foreskin as this will prevent chafe the skin protect the sensitive part underneath from injury and help to keep out germ therefore when blister be form do not tear off the skin insert a needle under the skin a little distance back from the blister and push it through to the opposite side press out the liquid through the hole thus form heat the needle red hot first with a match or candle to kill the germ when the skin be break -lrb- in cut and wound -rrb- keep the opening cover with a bandage to keep out germ and dirt otherwise the sore may fester pus be always cause by germ keep you hair short long hair and a long beard in the field generally mean a dirty head and a dirty face and favor skin disease louse and dandruff do not let any part of the body become chill as this very often be the direct cause of diarrhea dysentery pneumonia rheumatism and other disease wet clothes may be worn while march or exercise without bad result but there be great danger if one rest in wet clothing as the body may become chill do not sit or lie or sleep directly on damp ground as this be sure to chill the body when hot or perspiring or when wear damp clothes do not remain where a breeze can strike you you be sure to become chill every day if possible hang you blanket and clothing out to air in the sun shake or beat they with a small stick germ and vermin do not like this treatment but damp musty clothing suit they very well wash you shirt underwear and sock frequently the danger of blood poisoning from a wound be greatly increase if the bullet pass through dirty clothes ditch you tent as soon as you can particularly a shelter tent even if you camp for one night only otherwise a little rain may ruin a whole night 's rest always prepare you bed before dark level off the ground and scrape out a little hollow for you hip get some straw or dry grass if possible green grass or branch from tree be better than nothing sleep on you poncho this keep the dampness from come up from the ground and chill the body every minute spend in make a good bed mean about a hour 's good rest later on avoid the food and drink find for sale in the cheap stand about camp the quality be generally bad and it be often prepare in filthy place by very dirty person the use of intoxicating liquor be particularly dangerous in the field its excessive use even at long interval break down one 's system drinking man be more apt to get sick and less liable to get well than be they more sober comrade if alcohol be take at all it be best after the work of the day be over it should never be take when the body be expose to severe cold as it diminish the resistance of the body hot tea or coffee be much preferable under these circumstance care of the foot a soldier can not march with sore foot and march be the main part of a infantryman 's daily duty in the field all soldier should be familiar with the proper method of care for the foot sore foot be generally due to carelessness neglect or ignorance on the part of the soldier the most important factor in the care of the foot and the march ability of the soldier be the shoe civilian shoe particularly light patent leather or low shoe be sure to cause injury and in time will ruin a man 's foot only the march shoe issue by the quartermaster corps should be worn and they must be properly fit to the individual it will not suffice to order a march shoe of the same size as one 's ordinary civilian shoe for it must be remember that a soldier may have to march many mile daily over rough road and carry a heavy pack the pack itself cause the foot to spread out to a larger size and the rough road give so much exercise to the muscle of the foot that they swell greatly through the increase blood supply -lrb- for direction as to measure the foot for the march shoe see general order no 26 war department 1912 a copy of which should be on hand in each company -rrb- do not start out on a march wear new shoe this be a frequent cause of sore foot new shoe should be properly break in before begin a march by wear they for several hour daily for a week before the march and they should be adapt to the contour of the foot by stretch they with shoe stretcher with adjustable knob to take the pressure off painful corn and bunion such stretcher be issue by the quartermaster corps and there should be one or more pair in every company of infantry should this be impracticable then the follow be suggest : the soldier stand in he new shoe in about 2-1\/2 inch of water for about five minute until the leather be thoroughly pliable and moist he should then walk for about a hour on a level surface let the shoe dry on he foot to the irregularity of which the leather be thus mold in the same way as it be previously mold over the shoe last on take the shoe off a very little neat 's - foot oil should be rub into the leather to prevent its hardening and crack if it be desire to waterproof shoe at any time a considerable amount of neat 's - foot oil should be rub into the leather waterproof leather cause the foot of some man to perspire unduly and keep they constantly soft light woolen or heavy woolen sock will habitually be wear for march cotton sock will not be worn unless specifically order by the surgeon the sock will be large enough to permit free movement of the toe but not so loose as to permit of wrinkle darned sock or sock with hole in they will not be worn in march until the foot have harden they should be dust with foot powder which can be obtain at the regimental infirmary before each day 's march clean sock should be worn daily as soon as possible after reach camp after a day of march the foot should be wash with soap and water and the soldier should put on a dry pair of sock and he extra pair of shoe from he surplus kit if the skin be tender or the foot perspire wash with warm salt water or alum water but do not soak the foot a long time as this although very comforting at the time tend to keep they soft should blister 's appear on the foot prick and evacuate they by prick at the lower edge with a pin which have be pass through the flame of a match and cover they with zinc oxide plaster apply hot this plaster can be obtain on request at the regimental infirmary if serious abrasion appear on the foot or corn bunion and ingrow nail cause trouble have you name place on sick report and apply to the surgeon for treatment cut the toe nail square -lrb- fairly close in the middle but leave the side somewhat longer -rrb- as this prevent ingrow nail chapter v extract from infantry drill regulation unite state army 1911 -lrb- correct to April 15 1917 -rrb- section 1 definition alignment : a straight line upon which several element be form or be to be form or the dress of several element upon a straight line base : the element on which a movement be regulate battle sight : the position of the rear sight when the leaf be lay down center : the middle point or element of a command column : a formation in which the element be place one behind another deploy : to extend the front in general to change from column to line or from close order to extend order depth : the space from head to rear of any formation include the lead and rear element the depth of a man be assume to be 12 inch distance : space between element in the direction of depth distance be measure from the bark of the man in front to the breast of the man in rear the distance between rank be 40 inch in both line and column element : a file squad platoon company or larger body form part of a still larger body file : two man the front-rank man and the corresponding man of the rear rank the front-rank man be the file leader a file which have no rear-rank man be a blank file the term file apply also to a single man in a single-rank formation file closer : such officer and noncommissioned officer of a company as be post in rear of the line for convenience all man post in the line of file closer flank : the right or left of a command in line or in column : also the element on the right or left of the line formation : arrangement of the element of a command the placing of all fraction in they order in line in column or for battle front : the space in width occupy by a element either in line or in column the front of a man be assume to be 22 inch front also denote the direction of the enemy guide : a officer noncommissioned officer or private upon whom the command or element thereof regulate its march head : the lead element of a column interval : space between element of the same line the interval between man in rank be 4 inch and be measure from elbow to elbow between company squad etc it be measure from the left elbow of the left man or guide of the group on the right to the right elbow of the right man or guide of the group on the left left : the left extremity or element of a body of troops line : a formation in which the different element be abreast of each other order close : the formation in which the unit in double rank be arrange in line or in column with normal interval and distance order extend : the formation in which the unit be separate by interval greater than in close order pace : thirty inch the length of the full step in quick time point of rest : the point at which a formation begin specifically the point toward which unit be align in successive movement rank : a line of man place side by side right : the right extremity or element of a body of troops part i -- drill section 2 -- introduction 1 -lrb- 4 -rrb- success in battle be the ultimate object of all military training success may be look for only when the training be intelligent and thorough -lrb- footnote 4 : the number refer to paragraph in the infantry drill regulation 1911 -rrb- 2 commanding officer be accountable for the proper training of they respective organization within the limit prescribe by regulation and order the excellence of a organization be judge by its field efficiency the field efficiency of a organization depend primarily upon its effectiveness as a whole thoroughness and uniformity in the training of the unit of a organization be indispensable to the efficiency of the whole it be by such means alone that the requisite teamwork may be develop 3 simple movement and elastic formation be essential to correct training for battle 4 the drill regulation be furnish as a guide they provide the principle for training and for increase the probability of success in battle in the interpretation of the regulation the spirit must be seek quibble over the minutiæ of form be indicative of failure to grasp the spirit 5 the principle of combat be consider in part ii of these regulation they be treat in the various school include in part i only to the extent necessary to indicate the function of the various commander and the division of responsibility between they the amplification necessary to a proper understanding of they application be to be seek in part ii 6 the follow important distinction must be observe : -lrb- a -rrb- drill execute at attention and the ceremony be disciplinary exercise design to teach precise and soldierly movement and to inculcate that prompt and subconscious obedience which be essential to proper military control to this end smartness and precision should be exact in the execution of every detail such drill should be frequent but short -lrb- b -rrb- the purpose of extended order drill be to teach the mechanism of deployment of the firing and in general of the employment of troops in combat such drill be in the nature of disciplinary exercise and should be frequent thorough and exact in order to habituate man to the firm control of they leader extend order drill be execute at ease the company be the largest unit which execute extended order drill -lrb- c -rrb- field exercise be for instruction in the duty incident to campaign assume situation be employ each exercise should conclude with a discussion on the ground of the exercise and principle involve -lrb- d -rrb- the combat exercise a form of field exercise of the company battalion and larger unit consist of the application of tactical principle to assume situation employ in the execution the appropriate formation and movement of close and extended order combat exercise must simulate as far as possible the battle condition assume in order to familiarize both officer and man with such condition company and battalion will frequently be consolidate to provide war-strength organization officer and noncommissioned officer not require to complete the full quota of the unit participate be assign as observer or umpire the firing line can rarely be control by the voice alone thorough training to insure the proper use of prescribe signal be necessary the exercise should be follow by a brief drill at attention in order to restore smartness and control 7 in field exercise the enemy be say to be imaginary when he position and force be merely assume outline when he position and force be indicate by a few man represent when a body of troop act as such general rule for drill and formation 8 when the preparatory command consist of more than one part its element be arrange as follow : -lrb- 1 -rrb- for movement to be execute successively by the subdivision or element of a organization : -lrb- a -rrb- description of the movement -lrb- b -rrb- how execute or on what element execute -lrb- 2 -rrb- for movement to be execute for the execution of the movement toward either flank the substitute word of the command be place within parenthesis 10 any movement may be execute either from the halt or when march unless otherwise when not otherwise prescribe the other unit march in double time to they place in the formation order and then conform to the gait of the lead or base unit if march in double time the command double time be omit the lead or base unit march in quick time the other unit continue at double time to they place in the formation order and then conform to the gait of the lead or base unit 13 to hasten the execution of a movement begin in quick time the command : 1 _ double_time _ 2 march be give the lead or base unit continue to march in quick time or remain at a halt if already halt the other unit complete the execution of the movement in double time and then conform to the gait of the lead or base unit 14 to stay the execution of a movement when march for the correction of error the command : and insure steadiness and promptness in the rank 23 except at ceremony the special unit have no fixed place they take place as direct in the absence of direction they conform as nearly as practicable to the plate and in subsequent movement maintain they relative position with respect to the flank or end of the command on which they be originally post 24 general field and staff officer be habitually mount the staff of a officer form in single rank 3 pace in rear of he the right or the rank extend 1 pace to the right of a point directly in rear of he member of the staff be arrange in order from right to leave as follow : general staff officer adjutant aid other staff officer arrange in each classification in order of rank the senior on the right the flag of the general officer and the orderly be 3 pace in rear of the staff the flag on the right when necessary to reduce the front of the staff and orderly each line execute two right or fours right as explain in the cavalry drill regulation and follow the commander when not otherwise prescribe staff officer draw and return saber with they chief 25 in make the about a officer mount habitually turn to the leave when the commander face to give command the staff flag and orderly do not change position 26 when make or receive official report or on meet out of door all officer will salute military courtesy require the junior to salute first but when the salute be introductory to a report make at a military ceremony or formation to the representative of a common superior -lrb- as for example to the adjutant officer of the day etc -rrb- the officer make the report whatever he rank will salute first the officer to whom the report be make will acknowledge by salute that he have receive and understand the report 27 for ceremony all mount enlist man of a regiment or smaller unit except those belong to the machine-gun organization be consolidate into a detachment the senior present command if no officer be in drill at attention otherwise either a command signal or order be employ as best suit the occasion or one may he use in conjunction with another 32 signal should be freely use in instruction in order that officer and man may readily know they in make firm signal the saber rifle or headdress may be hold in the hand 33 officer and man fix they attention at the first word of command the first note of the bugle or whistle or the first motion of the signal a signal include both the preparatory command and the command of execution : the movement commence as soon as the signal be understand unless otherwise prescribe 34 except in movement execute at attention commander or leader of subdivision repeat order command or signal whenever such repetition be deem necessary to insure prompt and correct execution officer battalion noncommissioned staff officer platoon leader guide and musician be equip with whistle the major and he staff will use a whistle of distinctive tone the captain and company musician a second and distinctive whistle the platoon leader and guide a third distinctive whistle 35 prescribed signal be limit to such as be essential as a substitute for the voice under condition which render the voice inadequate before or during a engagement special signal may be agree upon to facilitate the solution of such special difficulty as the particular situation be likely to develop but it must be remember that simplicity and certainty be indispensable quality of a signal order 36 in these regulation a order embrace instruction or direction give orally or in write in term suit to the particular occasion and not prescribe herein order be employ only when the command prescribe herein do not sufficiently indicate the will of the commander order be more fully describe in paragraph 378 to 383 inclusive command 37 in these regulation a command be the will of the commander express in the phraseology prescribe herein 38 there be two kind of command : the preparatory command such as _ forward _ indicate the movement that be to be execute the command of execution such as march halt or arm cause the execution preparatory command be distinguish by _ italics _ those of execution by capital where it be not mention in the text who give the command prescribe they be to be give by the commander of the unit concern the preparatory command should be give at such a interval of time before the command of execution as to admit of be properly understand the command of execution should be give at the instant the movement be to commence the tone of command be animated distinct and of a loudness proportion to the number of man for whom it be intend each preparatory command be enunciate distinctly with a rise inflection at the end and in such manner that the command of execution may he more energetic the command of execution be firm in tone and brief 39 major and commander of unit larger than a battalion repeat such command of they superior as be to be execute by they unit face they unit for that purpose the battalion be the largest unit that execute a movement at the command of execution of its commander 40 when give command to troops it be usually best to face toward they indifference in give command must be avoid as it lead to laxity in execution command should be give with spirit at all time bugle signal 41 the authorize bugle signal be publish in part v of these regulation the following bugle signal may be use off the battle field when not likely to convey information to the enemy : attention : troops be bring to attention attention to order : troops fix they attention forward march : use also to execute quick time from double time double time march to the rear march : in close order execute squad right about halt assemble march the follow bugle signal may signal be equivalent to fire at will cease firing : all part of the line execute cease firing at once these signal be not use by unit smaller than a regiment except when such unit be independent or leave thumb extend along the stock muzzle at the height of the breast and turn the cut-off up with the right hand he turn and draw the bolt back take a loaded clip and insert the end in the clip slot without remove the clip thrust the bolt home turn down the handle turn the safety lock to the safe find carry the hand to the small of the stock each rear-rank man move to the right front take a hand steady and support the piece at the balance the toe of the butt rest on the ground the muzzle off the ground for reference these position -lrb- standing kneeling and lie down -rrb- be designate as that of load 140 for instruction in loading : 1 _ simulate _ 2 load execute as above describe except that the cut-off remain off and the handling of cartridge be simulated the recruit be first may be fill in whole or in part while off or on by press cartridge singly down and back until they be in the proper place the use of the rifle as a single loader be however to be regard as exceptional to unload 142 unload take the position of load turn the safety lock up and move bolt alternately back and forward until all the cartridge be eject after the last cartridge be eject the chamber be close by first thrust the bolt slightly forward to free it from the stud hold it in place when the chamber be open press the follower down and back to engage it under the bolt and then thrust the bolt home the trigger be pull the cartridge be then pick up clean and return to the belt and the piece be bring to the order to set the sight 143 range eleven hundred -lrb- eight-fifty etc -rrb- or battle
