until order to suspend or cease firing 147 to increase -lrb- decrease -rrb- the rate of fire in progress the instructor shout : faster -lrb- slower -rrb- man be train to fire at the rate of about three shot per minute at effective range and five or six at close range devote the minimum of time to load and the maximum to deliberate aim to illustrate the necessity for deliberation and to habituate man to combat condition small and comparatively indistinct target be designate to fire by clip 148 clip fire execute in the same manner we fire at will except that each man after have exhaust the cartridge then in the piece suspend firing to suspend firing 149 the instructor blow a long blast of the whistle and repeat same if necessary or command : suspend firing firing stop piece be hold loaded and lock in a position of readiness for instant resumption of firing rear sight unchanged the man continue to observe the target or aim point or the place at which the target disappear or at which it be expect to reappear this whistle signal may be use as a preliminary to cease firing to cease firing 150 cease firing firing stop piece not already there be bring to the position of load those not load be load sight be lay piece be lock and bring to the older cease firing be use for long pause to prepare for change of position or to steady the man 151 command for suspend or cease fire may be give at any time after the preparatory command for firing whether the firing have actually commence or not the use of cover 152 the recruit should be give careful instruction in the individual use of cover it should be impress upon he that in take advantage of natural cover he must be able to fire easily and effectively upon the enemy if advance on a enemy he must do so steadily and as rapidly as possible he must conceal himself as much as possible while firing and while advance while set he sight he should be under cover or lie prone 153 to teach he to fire easily and effectively at the same time conceal himself from the view of the enemy he be practice in simulated firing in the prone sit kneel and crouch position from behind hillock tree heap of earth or rock from depression gully ditch doorway or window he be teach to fire around the right side of he concealment whenever possible or when this be not possible to rise enough to fire over the top of he concealment when these detail be understand he be require to select cover with reference to a assume enemy and to place himself behind it in proper position for firing 154 the evil of remain too long in one place however good the concealment should be explain he should be teach to advance from cover to cover select cover in advance before leave he concealment it should be impress upon he that a man run rapidly toward all enemy furnish a poor target he should be train in spring from a prone position behind concealment run at top speed to cover and throw himself behind it he should also be practice in advance from cover to cover by crawl or by lie on the left side rifle grasp in the right hand and push himself forward with the right leg 155 he should be teach that when fire on while act independently he should drop to the ground seek cover and then endeavor to locate he enemy 156 the instruction of the recruit in the use of cover be continue in the combat exercise of the company but he must then be teach that the proper advance of the platoon or company and the effectiveness of its fire be of greater importance than the question of cover for individual he should also be teach that he may not move about or shift he position in the firing line except the better to see the target observation 157 the ability to use he eye accurately be of great importance to the soldier the recruit should be train in observe he surround from position and when on the march he should be practice in point out and name military feature of the ground in distinguish between live being in count distant group of object or being in recognize color and form 158 in the training of man in the mechanism of the firing line they should be practice in repeat to one another target and aim point designation and in quickly locate and point out a designate target they should be teach to distinguish from a prone position distant object particularly troops both with the naked eye and with field glass similarly they should be train in estimate distance section 6 school of the company 159 the captain be responsible for the theoretical and practical instruction of he officer and noncommissioned describe for the company the advance 212 the advance of a company into a engagement -lrb- whether for attack or defense -rrb- be conduct in close order preferably column of squad until the probability of encounter hostile fire make it advisable to deploy after deployment and before open fire the advance of the company may be continue in skirmish line or other suitable formation depend upon circumstance the advance may often be facilitate or better advantage take of cover or loss reduce by the employment of the platoon or squad column or by the use of a succession of thin line the selection of the method to be use be make by the captain or major the choice depend upon condition arise during the progress of the advance if the deployment be find to be premature it will generally be best to assemble the company and proceed in close order patrol ure use to provide the necessary security against surprise 213 be in skirmish line : 1 _ platoon_columns _ 2 march the platoon leader column be profitably use where the ground be so difficult or cover so limited as to make it desirable to take advantage of the few favorable route no two platoon should march within the area of burst of a single shrapnel -lrb- 5 -rrb- squad column be of value principally in facilitate the advance over rough or brush-grown ground they afford no material advantage in secure cover -lrb- footnote 5 : ordinarily about 20 yard wide -rrb- 216 to deploy platoon or squad column : 1 _ as_skirmishers _ 2 march skirmisher move to the right or left front and successively place themselves in they original indicate by the captain and to they place in line the company be re-formed in line 218 be in skirmish line to advance by a succession of thin line : 1 _ -lrb- such_numbers -rrb- _ forward _ 2 march the captain point out in advance the select position in front of the line occupy the designate number of each squad move to the front the line thus form preserve the original interval as nearly as practicable when this line have advance a suitable distance -lrb- generally from 100 to 250 yard depend upon the terrain and the character of the hostile fire -rrb- a second be send forward by similar command and so on at irregular distance until the whole line have advance upon arrive at the indicated position the first line be halt successive line upon arrive halt on line with the first and the man take they proper place in the skirmish line ordinarily each line be make up of one man per squad and the man of a squad be send forward in order from right to leave as deploy the first line be lead by the platoon leader of the right platoon the second by the guide of the right platoon and so on in order from right to leave the advance be conduct in quick time unless condition demand a faster gait the company have arrive at the indicated position a further advance by the same means may be advisable 219 the advance in a succession of thin line be use to cross a wide stretch sweep or likely to be sweep by artillery fire or heavy long-range rifle fire which can not profitably be return its purpose be the building up of a strong skirmish line preparatory to engage in a fire tight this method of advance result in serious -lrb- though temporary -rrb- loss of control over the company its advantage lie in the fact that it offer less definite target hence be less likely to draw fire 220 the above be suggestion other and better formation may be devise to fit particular case the best formation be the one which advance the line farthest with the least loss of man time and control the fire attack 221 the principle govern the advance of the firing line in attack be consider in the school of the battalion when it become impracticable for the company to advance as a whole by ordinary means it advance by rush 222 be in skirmish line : 1 _ by_platoon _ -lrb- two_platoons_squad _ _ four_men_etc -rrb- _ from_the_right _ -lrb- left -rrb- _ 2 rush the platoon leader on the indicate flank carefully arrange the detail for a prompt and vigorous execution of the rush and put it into effect as soon as practicable if necessary he designate the leader for the indicate fraction when about to rush he cause the man of the fraction to cease firing and to hold themselves flat but in readiness to spring forward instantly the leader of the rush -lrb- at the signal of the platoon leader if the latter be not the leader of the rush -rrb- command : follow I and run at top speed lead the fraction to the new line where be halt it and cause it to open fire the leader of the rush select the new line if it have not be previously designate the first fraction have establish itself on the new line the next like fraction be send forward by its platoon leader without further command of the captain and so on successively until the entire company be on the line establish by the first rush if more than one platoon be to join in one rush the junior platoon leader conform to the action of the senior a part of the line have advance the captain may increase or decrease the size of the fraction to complete the movement 223 when the company form a part of the firing line the rush of the company as a whole be conduct by the captain as describe for a platoon in the precede paragraph the captain lead the rush platoon leader lead they respective platoon platoon guide follow the line to insure prompt and orderly execution of the advance 224 when the foregoing method of rush by run become impracticable any method of advance that bring the attack closer to the enemy such as crawl should be employ for regulation govern the charge see paragraph 318 and 319 the company in support 225 to enable it to follow or reach the firing line the support adopt suitable formation follow the principle explain in paragraph 212-218 the support should be keep assemble as long as practicable if after deploy a favorable opportunity arise to hold it for some time in close formation it should be reassemble it be redeploy when necessary 226 the movement of the support as a whole and the dispatch of reenforcement from it to the firing line be control by the major a reenforcement of less than one platoon have little influence and will be avoid whenever practicable the captain of a company in support be constantly on the alert for the major 's signal or command 227 a reenforcement send to the firing line join it deploy as skirmisher the leader of the reenforcement place it in a interval in the line if one exist : and command it thereafter as a unit if no such suitable interval exist the reenforcement be advance with increase interval between skirmisher each man occupy the nearest interval in the firing line and each then obey the order of the nearest squad lender and platoon leader 228 a reenforcement join the firing line as quickly as possible without exhaust the man 229 the original platoon division of the company in the firing line should be maintain and should not be break up by the mingling of reenforcement upon join the firing line officer and sergeant accompany a reenforcement take over the duty of other of like grade who have be disabled or distribute themselves so as best to exercise they normal function condition with vary and no rule can be prescribe it be essential that all assist in master the increase difficulty of control the company act alone 230 in general the company when act alone be employ accord to the principle applicable to the battalion act alone the captain employ platoon as the major employ company make due allowance for the difference in strength the support may be smaller in proportion or may be dispense with 231 the company must be well protect against surprise combat patrol on the flank be specially important each leader of a flank platoon detail a man to watch for the signal of the patrol or patrol on he flank fire 232 ordinarily piece be load and extra ammunition be issue before the company deploy for combat in close order the company execute the firing at the command of the captain who post himself in rear of the center of the company usually the firing in close order consist of salute volley only 233 when the company be deploy the man execute the firing at the command of they platoon leader the latter give such command as be necessary to carry out the captain 's direction and from time to time add such further command as be necessary to continue correct and control the fire order 234 the voice be generally inadequate for give command during fire and must be replace by signal of such character that proper fire direction and control be assure to attract attention signal must usually be precede by the whistle signal -lrb- short blast -rrb- a friction of the firing line about to rush should it practicable avoid use the long blast signal as a aid to cease firing officer and man behind the firing line can not ordinarily move freely along the line but must depend on mutual watchfulness and the proper use of the prescribe signal all should post themselves so as to see they immediate superior and subordinate 235 the musician assist the captain by observe the enemy the target and the fire effect by transmit command or signal and by watch for signal 236 firing with blank cartridge at a outline or represent enemy at distance less than 100 yard be prohibit 237 the effect of fire and the influence of the ground in relation thereto and the individual and collective instruction in marksmanship be treat in the small-arm firing manual range 238 for convenience of reference range be classify as follow : 0 to 600 yard close range 600 to 1200 yard effective range 1200 to 2000 yard long range 2000 yard and over distant range 239 the distance to the target must be determine as accurately as possible and the sight set accordingly aside from training and morale this be the most important single factor in secure effective fire at the longer range 240 except in a deliberately prepared defensive position the most accurate and only practicable method of determine the range will generally be to take the mean of several estimate five or six officer or man select from the most accurate estimator in the company be designate as range estimator and be specially train in estimate distance whenever necessary and practicable the captain assemble the range estimator point out the target to they and adopt the mean of they estimate the range estimator then take they customary post class of firing 241 volley firing have limit application in defense it may be use in the early stage of the action if the enemy present a large compact target it may be use by troops execute fire of position when the ground near the target be such that the strike of bullet can be see from the firing line range volley may be use to correct the sight setting in combat volley firing be execute habitually by platoon 242 fire at will be the class of fire normally employ in attack or defense 243 clip fire have limit application it be principally use : 1 in the early stage of combat to steady the man by habituate they to brief pause in firing 2 to produce a short burst of fire the target 244 ordinarily the major will assign to the company a objective in attack or sector in defense the company 's target will lie within the limit so assign in the choice of target tactical consideration be paramount the nearest hostile troops within the objective or sector will thus be the usual target this will ordinarily be the hostile firing line troops in rear be ordinarily proper target for artillery machine gun or at time infantry employ fire of position change of target should not be make without excellent reason therefor such as the sudden appearance of hostile troops under condition which make they more to be fear than the troops comprise the former target 245 the distribution of fire over the entire target be of special importance the captain allot a part of the target to each platoon or each platoon leader take as he target that part which correspond to he position in the company man be so instruct that each fire on that part of the target which be directly opposite he 246 all part of the target be equally important care must be exercise that the man do not slight its less visible part a section of the target not cover by fire represent a number of the enemy permit to fire cooly and effectively 247 if the target can not be see with the naked eye platoon leader select a object in front of or behind it designate this as the aim target and direct a sight setting which will carry the cone of fire into the target fire direction 248 when the company be large enough to be divide into platoon it be impracticable for the captain to command it directly in combat he efficiency in manage the firing line be measure by he ability to enforce he will through the platoon leader have indicate clearly what he desire they to do he avoid interfere except to correct serious error or omission 249 the captain direct the fire of the company or of designate platoon he designate the target and when practicable allot a part of the target to each platoon before begin the fire action he determine the range announce the sight setting and indicate the class of fire to be employ and the time to open fire thereafter he observe the fire effect correct material error in sight setting prevent exhaustion of the ammunition supply and cause the distribution of such extra ammunition as may be receive from the rear fire control 250 in combat the platoon be the fire unit from 20 to 35 rifle be as many as one leader can control effectively 251 each platoon leader put into execution the command or direction of the captain have first take such precaution to insure correct sight setting and clear description of the target or aim target as the situation permit or require thereafter he give such additional command or direction as be necessary to exact compliance with the captain 's will he correct the sight setting when necessary he designate a aim target when the target can not be see with the naked eye 252 in general platoon leader observe the target and the effect of they fire and be on the alert for the captain 's command or signal they observe and regulate the rate of fire the platoon guide watch the firing line and check every breach of fire discipline squad leader transmit command and signal when necessary observe the conduct of they squad and abate excitement assist in enforce fire discipline and participate in the firing 253 the best troops be those that submit longest to fire control loss of control be a evil which rob success of its greatest result to avoid or delay such loss should be the constant aim of all fire control imply the ability to stop firing change the sight setting and target and resume a well direct fire fire discipline 254 fire discipline imply besides a habit of obedience a control of the rifle by the soldier the result of training which will enable he in action to make hit instead of miss it embrace take advantage of the ground care in set the sight and delivery of fire constant attention to the order of the leader and careful observation of the enemy a increase of fire when the target be favorable and a cessation of fire when the enemy disappear economy of ammunition -lrb- small-arms firing manual -rrb- in combat shot which graze the enemy 's trench or position and thus reduce the effectiveness of he fire have the approximate value of hit such shot only or actual hit contribute toward fire superiority fire discipline imply that in a firing line without leader each man retain he presence of mind and direct effective fire upon the proper target 255 to create a correct appreciation of the requirement of fire discipline man be teach that the rate of fire should be as rapid as be consistent with accurate aim that the rate will depend upon the visibility proximity and size or the target and that the proper rate will ordinarily suggest itself to each trained man usually render caution or command unnecessary in attack the highest rate of fire be employ at the halt precede the assault and in pursue fire 256 in a advance by rush leader of troops in firing position be responsible for the delivery of heavy fire to cover the advance of each rush fraction troops be train to change slightly the direction of fire so as not to endanger the flank of advanced portion of the firing line 257 in defense when the target disappear behind cover platoon leader suspend fire prepare they platoon to fire upon the point where it be expect to reappear and greet its reappearance instantly with vigorous fire section 7 company inspection 745 be in line at a halt : 1 _ open_ranks _ 2 march at the command the right-rear corner this fold the right side of the tent on itself with the crease in the middle and under the front side of tent next carry the left-front corner to the right and back as describe above this when complete will leave the front and rear side of the tent lie smooth and fiat and the two side wall fold inward each on itself place the hood in the square iron which have be fold instruction be to teach the soldier how to make effect use of the rifle and bayonet in personal combat : to make he quick and proficient in handle he rifle to give he a accurate eye and a steady hand and to give he confidence in the bayonet in offense and defense when skill in these exercise have be acquire the rifle will still remain a most formidable weapon at close quarter should the bayonet be lose or disabled 3 efficiency of organization in bayonet fighting will be judge by the skill show by individual in personal combat for this purpose pair or group of opponent select at random from among recruit and trained soldier should engage in assault use the fencing equipment provide for the purpose 4 officer and specially select and thoroughly instruct noncommissioned officer will act we instructor 5 instruction in bayonet combat should begin as soon as the soldier be familiar with the handling of he rifle and will progress as far as practicable in the order follow in the text 6 instruction be ordinarily give on even ground but practice should also be have on uneven ground especially in the attack and defense of intrenchment 7 these exercise will not be use as a calisthenic cadence as the attempt to do so result in incomplete execution and lack of vigor each movement will be execute correctly as quickly as possible by every man as soon as the movement be execute accurately the command be give rapidly as expertness with the bayonet depend chiefly upon quickness of motion 10 the exercise will he interrupt at first by short and frequent rest the rest will be less frequent as proficiency be attain fatigue and exhaustion will be specially guard against as they prevent proper interest be take in the exercise and delay the progress of the instruction rest bayonet iv combine movement 46 the purpose of combined movement be to develop more vigorous attack and more effective defens than be obtain by the single movement to develop skill in pass from attack to defense and the reverse every movement to the front should be accompany by a attack which be increase in effectiveness by the forward movement of the body every movement to the rear should ordinarily be accompany by a parry and should always be follow by a attack movement to the right or left may be accompany by attack or defense 47 not more than three movement will be use in any principle of practical bayonet combat should be teach as far as possible during the progress of instruction in bayonet exercise 50 the soldier must be continually impress with the extreme importance of the offensive due to its moral effect should a attack fail it should be follow immediately by another attack before the opponent have a opportunity to assume the offensive keep the opponent on the defensive if due to circumstance it be necessary to take the defensive constantly watch for a opportunity to assume the offensive and take immediate advantage of it 51 observe the ground with a view to obtain the best footing time for this will generally be too limited to permit more than a single hasty glance 52 in personal combat watch the opponent 's eye if they can be plainly see and do not fix the eye on he weapon nor upon the point of you attack if he eye can not be plainly see as in night attack watch the movement of he weapon and of he body 53 keep the body well cover and deliver attack vigorously the point of the bayonet should always be keep as nearly as possible in the line of attack the less the rifle be move upward downward to the right or to the leave the better prepare the soldier be for attack or defense 54 constantly watch for a chance to attack the opponent 's left hand he position of guard will not differ materially from that describe in paragraph 24 if he bayonet be without a cut edge he will be at a great disadvantage 55 the butt be use for close and sudden attack it be particularly useful in riot duty from the position of port arm a sentry can strike a severe blow with the butt of the rifle 56 against a man on foot arm with a sword be careful that the muzzle of the rifle be not grasp all the swordsman 's energy will be direct toward get past the bayonet attack he with short stab thrust and keep he beyond striking distance of he weapon 57 the adversary may attempt a greater extension in the thrust and lunge by quit the grasp of he piece with the left hand and advance the right as far as possible when this be do a sharp parry may cause he to lose control of he rifle leave he expose to a counter attack which should follow promptly 58 against odds a small number of man can fight to best advantage by group themselves so as to prevent they be attack from behind 59 in fight a mount man arm with a saber every effort must be make to get on he near or left side because here he reach be much shorter and he parry much weaker if not possible to disable such a enemy attack he horse and then renew the attack on the horseman 60 in receive night attack the assailant 's movement can be best observe from the kneel or prone position as he approach generally bring he against the sky line when he arrive within attack distance rise quickly and lunge well forward at the middle of he body vi fencing exercise 61 fencing exercise in two line consist of combination of thrust parry and foot movement execute at command or at will the opponent reply with suitable parry and return 62 the instructor will inspect the entire fencing equipment before the exercise begin and fissure himself that everything be in such condition as will prevent accident 63 the man equip themselves and form in two line at the order face each other with interval of about 4 pace between file and a distance of about 2 pace between line one line be designate as number 1 the other number 2 also as attack and defense 64 the opponent be at the order face each other the instructor command : salute each man with eye on he opponent carry the left hand smartly to the right side palm of the hand down thumb and finger extend and join forearm horizontal forefinger touch the bayonet -lrb- two -rrb- drop the arm smartly by the side this salute be the fencing salute all fencing exercise and all fencing at will between individual will begin and terminate with the formal courtesy of the fencing salute 65 after the fencing salute have be render the instructor command : 1 _ fencing_exercise _ 2 guard at the command guard each man come to the position of guard heretofore define bayonet cross each man 's bayonet bearing lightly to the right against the corresponding portion of the opponent 's bayonet this position be know as the engage or engage right 66 be at the engage right : engage leave the attack drop the point of he bayonet quickly until clear of he opponent 's rifle and describe a semicircle with it upward and to the right bayonet be cross similarly as in the engage position each man 's bayonet bearing lightly to the leave against the corresponding portion of the opponent 's bayonet 67 be at engage left : engage right the attack quickly drop the point of he bayonet until clear of he opponent 's rifle and describe a semicircle with it upward and to the left and engage 68 be engage : engage left and right the attack engage left and then immediately engage right 69 be engage left : engage right and leave the attack engage right and then immediately engage left 70 1 number one engage right -lrb- left -rrb- 2 number two counter number one execute the movement order as above number two quickly drop the point of he bayonet and circle it upward to the original position 71 in all fencing while maintain the pressure in the engage a certain freedom of motion of the rifle be allowable consist of the play or up-and-down number two initiate the movement number one thrust as soon as the opening be make and number two then attempt to parry 79 a counter attack or return be one make instantly after or in continuation of a parry the parry should be as narrow as possible this make it more difficult for the opponent to recover and counter parry the counter attack should also be make at or just before the full extension of the opponent 's attack as when it be so make a simple extension of the arm will generally be sufficient to reach the opponent 's body example : be at engage 1 number two at chest lunge 2 number one engage 1 number one press and at chest thrust 2 number two parry right 3 assault 82 the attack by disengagement be particularly effective follow the press example : be at the engage 1 number one press and at stomach thrust 2 number two low parry left 3 assault 83 the beat be a attack in which a sharp blow be strike against the opponent 's rifle for the purpose of force he to expose a opening into which a attack immediately follow it be use when there be but slight opposition or no contact of rifle example : be at the engage 1 number one beat and at stomach -lrb- chest etc -rrb- thrust 2 number require superior strength on the part of the attack example : be at the engage 1 number one twist and at stomach thrust 2 number two low parry left 3 assault feint 85 feint be movement which threaten or simulate attack and be make with a view to induce a opening or parry that expose the desire point of attack they be either single or double accord to the number of such movement make by the attack 86 in order that the attack may be change quickly as little force as possible be put into a feint example : be at the engage 1 number one feint head thrust at stomach lunge 2 number two parry right and low parry right 3 assault number one execute the feint and then the attack number two execute both parry 87 in double feint first one part of the body and then another be threaten and a third instructor will proceed to the exercise at will by which be mean assault between two man each endeavor to hit the other and to avoid be hit himself fencing at will should not be allow to degenerate into random attack and defens 97 the instructor can supervise but one pair of combatant at a time frequent change should be make so that the man may earn different method of attack and defense from each other 98 the contest should begin with simple careful movement with a view to form a correct opinion of the adversary afterwards everything will depend on coolness rapid and correct execution of the movement and quick perception of the adversary 's intention 99 continual retreat from the adversary 's attack and frequent dodge to escape attack should be avoid the offensive should he continually encourage 100 in fencing at will when no command be give opponent face each other at the position of order arm salute they then immediately and simultaneously assume the position of guard rifle engage neither man may take the position of guard before he opponent have complete he salute the choice of position be decide before the salute 101 the opponent be about two pace apart and the fencing salute have be render the instructor command 1 _ at _ _ will _ 2 assault after which either party have the right to attack to interrupt the contest the instructor will command halt at which the combatant will immediately come to the order to terminate the contest the instructor will command 1 _ halt _ 2 salute at which the combatant will immediately come to the order salute and remove they mask 102 when man have acquire confidence in fencing at will one opponent should be require to advance upon the other in quick time at charge bayonet from a distance not to exceed 10 yard and deliver a attack as soon as a hit be make by either opponent the instructor command halt and the assault terminate opponent alternate in assault the assailant be likewise require to advance at double time from a distance not exceed 20 yard and at a run from a distance not exceed 30 yard 103 the instructor will closely observe the contest and decide doubtful point he will at once stop the contest upon the slightest indication of temper after conclusion of the combat he will comment on the action of both party point out error and deficiency and explain how they may be avoid in the future 104 as additional instruction the man may be permit to wield the rifle leave hand that be on the left side of the body leave hand at the small of the stock many man will be able to use this method to advantage it be also of value in case the left band be wound -lrb- illustration : par 104 -rrb- 105 after man have fence in pair practice should be give in fencing between group equally and unequally divide when practicable intrenchment will be use in fencing of this character in group fencing it will be necessary to have a sufficient number of umpire to decide hit a individual receive a hit be withdraw at once from the bout which be decide in favor of the group have the numerical superiority at the end the fencing salute be not require in group fencing rule for fencing at will 106 1 hit on the leg below the knee will not be count no hit count unless in the opinion of the instructor it have sufficient force to disable 2 upon receive a hit call out hit 3 after receive a fair hit a counter attack be not permit a position of engage be take 4 a second or third hit in a combined attack will be count only when the first hit be not call 5 when it be necessary to stop the contest -- for example because of breaking of weapon or displacement of means of protection -- take the position of the order 6 when it be necessary to suspend the assault for any cause it will not be resume until the adversary be ready and in condition to defend himself 7 attack direct at the crotch be prohibit in fencing 8 step out of bound when establish count as a hit suggestion for fencing at will 107 when engage in a assault first study the adversary 's position and proceed by false attack execute with speed to discover if possible he instinctive parry in order to draw the adversary out and induce he to expose that part of the body at which the attack be to be make it be advisable to simulate a attack by a feint and then make the real attack 108 return attack should be frequently practice as they be difficult to parry and the opponent be within easier reach and more expose the return can be make a continuation of the parry as there be no previous warning of its delivery although it should always be expect return be make without lunge if the adversary can be reach by thrust or cut 109 endeavor to overcome the tendency to make a return without know where it will hit make return blindly be a bad habit and lead to instinctive return -- that be habitual return with certain attack from certain parry -- a fault which the skilled opponent will soon discover 110 do not draw the rifle back preparatory to thrust and lunge 111 the purpose of fencing at will be to teach the soldier as many form of simple effective attack and defens as possible complicated and intricate movement should not be attempt hint for instructor 112 the influence of the instructor be great he must be master of he weapon not only to show the various movement but also to lead in the exercise at will he should stimulate the zeal of the man and arouse pleasure in the work officer should qualify themselves as instructor by fence with each other 113 the character of each man he bodily conformation and he degree of skill must always be take into account when the instructor be demonstrate the combination feint return and parry the rapidity of he attack should be regulate by the skill of the pupil and no more force than be necessary should be use if the pupil expose himself too much in the feint and parry the instructor will by a attack convince he of he error but if these return be too swiftly or too strongly make the pupil will become overcautious and the precision of he attack will be impaired the object be to teach the pupil not to give exhibition of superior skill 114 occasionally the instructor should leave himself uncovered and fail to parry in order to teach the pupil to take quick advantage of such opportunity suggestion instruction in bayonet exercise and bayonet fencing should be conduct with a view to teach the aggressive use of the bayonet unless troops be so thoroughly train with the bayonet that they believe that with it they be superior to they opponent it will be difficult or impossible to develop that morale which be necessary for a successful assault man should be impress with the importance of act always on the offensive in bayonet combat of push they attack with all they might troops which be successful in they first few bayonet encounter will seldom thereafter be call upon to use the bayonet -- they opponent will not await the assault chapter vi field service section 1 principle of infantry training inaction give every advantage to the enemy the offensive alone give decisive result a quick and energetic offensive minimize loss a advance against the enemy 's position once enter upon must be continue to go back under fire be to die the best way to hold down the fire of the enemy and to diminish he power to inflict loss be to bring the position he occupy under well conduct and continue fire present as small a target as possible to the enemy by utilize every bit of cover the ground afford individual skill in marksmanship be a advantage in battle only when unite with fire discipline and control constant movement to the front lessen the effect of the enemy 's fire modern battle fight in the open show that the heaviest loss be in the mid and long range when close range be reach the loss diminish rapidly the best protection against artillery fire be a constant but irregular movement to the front when close to the enemy 's position he fire be least effective a knowledge of how to use the bayonet and the will to use it must often be the decide factor in battle finally : in infantry training we can not go far wrong or fail to accomplish the best result if we keep before we mind the spirit as well as the wording of paragraph 352 of the infantry drill regulation : the duty of infantry be many and difficult all infantry must be fit to cope with all condition that may arise modern war require but one kind of infantry -- good infantry section 2 combat the field of battle be the final test of the instruction discipline and efficiency of the fight force of any army the battalion be the attack unit or the defense unit whether operating alone or as part of a regiment the company constitute the firing line and the support a individual soldier be concern only with the enemy in he immediate front in obey order and instinctively do what he have be train to do the one requisite necessary to win the battle be intelligent team work the army be handle just like a football team a part be on the first line face the enemy another part like the half back be hold back as support another part like the full back be hold as a reserve each unit like each player have a certain duty to perform when the signal be give all work together -- all play the game -- team work the player consist of all branch of the service the same rule hold true down to the smallest unit and even to the individual enlist man each regiment be a team compose of three player -- each a battalion each battalion be a team of four player -- each a company in the same manner each company be a team of two or more platoon each platoon a team of two or more squad and last but not least each squad be a team of eight player the one question that always present itself on the battlefield every minute of the time to every person whether he be a general or a private be what play have my team captain order and how best may i act so as to work in conjunction with the other player to bring about the desire result -- team play to the infantry private this mean -- first prompt and loyal obedience to the squad leader every squad always have a team captain if the squad leader be kill or disabled another player previously designate take he place if no one be designate then the private with the longest service take command when the squad leader give the command for a certain play do not stop to think if the play be a good one but do you very best to carry ont the play as order a poor play in which every player enter with he whole heart -lrb- team work -rrb- will often win while on the other hand the best play in which some of the player be skulker and shirker will probably fail second never lose touch with you squad every individual as well as every unit should always be act under the control of some higher commander this be necessary if there be to be any unity of action therefore if you lose you squad or it become break up join the first squad you can find and obey you new squad leader as loyally and as cheerfully as you do you own infantry approach the battle field in column of squad while yet several mile from the enemy 's position the troops may come under artillery fire on green man enter upon they fight the sound of the projectile whistle through the air the noise flash and smoke on the burst of the shrapnel and the hum of the various piece thereafter all produce a very terrifying effect but old soldier soon learn to pay little attention to this as the danger be not great as the troops advance the column break up into smaller column which form on a irregular line with more or less interval between as the advance continue each column break up into smaller column until finally a line of skirmisher be form firing be delay as long as possible for three reason viz : -lrb- a -rrb- at the extreme range little damage can be do on the enemy and ineffective firing always encourage he -lrb- b -rrb- halt to fire delay the advance and the great object to be accomplish be to close in on the enemy where you can meet he on better term -lrb- c -rrb- plenty of ammunition will be require at the decisive stage of the fight and it be very difficult to send extra ammunition up to the firing line therefore never fire until order to do so and then never fire more than the number of round designate never fire after the command cease firing be give ammunition in the bandoleer will ordinarily be expend first thirty round in the right pocket section of the belt will be hold as a reserve to be expend only when order by a officer soon however it will be necessary to halt and open fire on the enemy in order to cause he some loss to make he rifleman keep down in they trench and to make they fire wildly it be probable that at this time and until you arrive much closer you will not see any of the enemy to fire at you may not even see any trench nor know just where the enemy be you higher officer however with they field glass and the message they receive will know each company will be assign a certain front to cover with its fire therefore be careful to fix you sight at the designate range and fire only at the designate target this mean team work in firing which be one of the most important element of success the firing line advance from position to position by means of rush at long range the entire line may rush forward at the same time but as the range decrease one part of the line rush forward while the remainder keep up a hot fire on the enemy the number take part in each rush decrease as the fire of the enemy become warmer until perhaps only one squad or even less rush or crawl forward at a time protect by the fire of the rest of the company the distance cover by each rush also become less and less after any rush no part of the line again advance until the rest of the line be up in make a rush the leader of the unit give the signal and lead the way the rest follow no attempt be make to keep a line but each man rush forward at a run seek only to reach the new halting position as quickly and with as little exposure as possible when halt the skirmisher need not be in a perfect line but every advantage should be take of the ground for concealment and protection it be necessary only that no man or group of man should interfere with the fire of other part of the firing line the noise on the firing line will be great leader will be disabled and new man will take they place reinforcement come up will cause unit to become mixed to the green man everything may appear to be in confusion but this be not so this be war as it really be if you have lose you squad or you squad leader join the leader nearest to you this be the way the game be play as long as the fight last every available rifleman must be keep in the firing line the first and last consideration be to win the battle therefore under no circumstance will any soldier be permit to go to the rear either for ammunition or to assist the wound if the attack force can no longer advance it be much safer to throw up hasty intrenchment and await the arrival of reinforcement or darkness than it be to retreat retreat troops be the one that suffer the greatest this lesson be teach by every great war therefore always remember that the safest thing to do be to stick to firing line troops on the firing line when not actually engage in firing at the enemy busy themselves throw up shelter trench it only require a few minute to construct a trench that give great protection therefore never get separate from you intrenching tool concealment be no less important than protection therefore when condition permit as be generally the case when on the defensive every effort should be make to hide intrenchment by the use of sod grass weed bush etc in make a attack the infantry be always support when possible by its own artillery which continue to fire over its head until the infantry arrive very close to the enemy 's trench this fire be help you a great deal by keep down the fire of the enemy infantry and artillery therefore do not think you be be fire into by you own artillery because you hear they shell and shrapnel singing through the air or burst a short distance in you front but rather be thankful you be receive they help up to the very last minute in the last rush which carry the enemy 's position there be always much mix of unit the firing line do not continue rush madly as individual after the enemy but halt and fire on he until he get out of good range the pursuit be take up by form troops hold in reserve or by the firing line only after its unit be again get together as the fighting often last all day and great suffering be cause from thirst do not throwaway you canteen when the fight commence it may also be impossible to get ration up to the line during the night therefore it be advisable to hold onto at least one ration as the recent war have show the possibility of hand-to-hand fighting especially at night each soldier should be school in the use of the bayonet the following have particular reference to the duty of platoon and squad leader and to the team work of the platoon in combat : attack troops must first gain fire superiority in order to reach the hostile position by gain fire superiority be mean make one 's fire superior to that of the enemy in volume and accuracy and it depend upon the number of rifle employ the rate of fire the character of the target training and discipline and fire direction and control when the fire of the attacker become effective and superior to that of the defender the latter be no longer able to effectively and coolly aim and fire at the former and as a consequence the attacker be able to inaugurate a successful rush or advance which carry they nearer to the enemy 's position when a trained organization have be commit to the attack the gain of fire superiority depend upon the way in which fire direction and fire control be exercise the captain direct the fire of the company he indicate to the platoon commander the target -lrb- enemy -rrb- which the company be to fire and advance upon and tell each upon which part of this target he be to direct the fire of he platoon when he desire the fire to be open he give the necessary command or signal include the range at which the sight lira to be set when the fire fight have once start it become to a great extent a fight of a number of platoon the platoon be the largest organization which can be control by a single leader in action the platoon commander -lrb- lieutenant or sergeant -rrb- control its fire in order to gain the maximum fire effect and to avoid waste ammunition he must try he best to make the fire of he platoon effective to get it forward and to support neighbor platoon in they effort to advance at the same time he must hold himself subject to he captain 's direction he should take advantage of every chance to carry he platoon forward unless otherwise order in all this he be assist by he platoon guide -lrb- sergeant -rrb- and by he corporal at the commencement of a engagement the platoon commander will give the objective -lrb- part of the enemy 's line or aim target -rrb- at which he platoon be to direct its fire noncommissioned officer must be sure that they see and understand the objective and that all the man in they squad do likewise fire be then direct at this objective without further command until the platoon commander give a new objective man should be instruct to aim at that part of the target assign to they platoon which correspond with they own position in they own platoon so that there will be no portion of the target which be not cover by fire a portion of the enemy 's line not cover by fire mean that that portion be able to coolly aim and fire at they opponent in a engagement the voice can seldom be hear over a few foot and the platoon commander will generally have to convey he order by signal a corporal may be able to shout order to he squad and order may be repeat along a skirmish line by shout care should be take that order intend for one platoon only be not thus convey to another platoon a short blast on the whistle give by the platoon commander mean attention to order all noncommissioned officer at once suspend firing and glance toward the platoon commander to see if the latter have any signal or order for they if not they resume firing a long blast on the whistle means suspend firing when a noncommissioned officer hear this signal from he platoon commander he should at once shout suspend firing upon receive a signal the noncommissioned officer for whom it be intend should at once repeat it back to be sure that it be correctly understand when a leader in command of a platoon or squad receive a order or signal to rush he should cause he man to suspend firing and to hold themselves flat but ready for a sprinter 's start he select the point as far as possible with reference to cover to which he intend to carry he unit forward he then give the command rush spring forward and run at full speed about three pace ahead of he man lead they in the rush arrive at the position he have select he throw himself prone and the man drop on either side of he all crawl forward to good firing position consider the cover also and the leader give the necessary order for resume the fire the latter will include give the range again the length of the rush be subtract from the sight set order at the last position as a rule rush should be start by a unit on one flank and should be follow in succession by the other unit to the opposite flank each succeed unit should halt on the line establish by the unit which first rush when a unit be about to rush leader in charge of adjacent unit should caution they man to be careful not to fire into the rush unit as it bound forward when one unit suspend fire for the purpose of rush adjacent leader should arrange to have a portion of they man turn they fire on the target of the rush unit to the end that there may be no portion of the enemy 's line not under fire and able to fire coolly on the rush unit rush should be make for as long a distance as possible due regard be have for the wind of the man and not to get beyond support distance of the other unit long rush facilitate a advance and quickly place a skirmish line close to the enemy 's position where its fire will have more effect a attack line suffer less from casualty at short range than it do at mid range every advantage should be take to utilize the cover available the best kind of cover be that which while it mask the skirmisher from the sight and fire of the enemy afford favorable condition for firing and for readily advance in order to allow man to regain they wind or should the fire of the enemy be so effective as to prevent a further advance without reinforcement advantage may be take to lie close in cover or hasty fire trench may be throw up in order to allow the line to maintain its position to go back under fire be to die when a platoon be firing all noncommissioned officer watch every opportunity to make the fire more effective the platoon guide should constantly watch the man to see that they do not become excited fire too hastily or without aim that they sight be set at the correct range that they be obviously firing at the designate target and that they assume steady firing position and take advantage of cover in perform these duty it may be necessary for the guide to be constantly crawl along the line a corporal in like manner supervise he squad firing with it when he be not actively engage in control it bayonet be fix preparatory to a charge this command be usually give by the bugle only one or two man in each squad should fix they bayonet at the same time in order that there may be no marked pause or diminution in the fire at this critical stage of the engagement in order to be effective in combat the platoon must be thoroughly train to work as a team each noncommissioned officer must be conversant with the signal and command and the proper method for instantly put into effect the order of he platoon commander each private must be train until he instinctively do the right thing in each phase of the action section 3 patrolling the designation of a patrol indicate the nature of the duty for which it be detail as for example visit reconnoiter explore flanking combat harass pursue etc a infantry patrol consist as a rule of from 3 to 16 man reconnoiter patrol be habitually small and seek safety in concealment or flight fight only when they mission demand it the most skillful reconnaissance be where patrol accomplish they mission and return without be discover by the enemy when resistance be expect stronger detachment be require these cover themselves with small patrol of two to four man the remainder act as support the commander determine the number and strength of patrol and when they be to be send out it be a cardinal principle to send out patrol of such strength only as will accomplish the object the officer send out the patrol verify the detail designate a second in command and give the necessary instruction the order or instruction for a patrol or for any detachment go on reconnoissance must state clearly where the enemy be or be suppose to be what information be desire what feature be of special importance the general direction to be follow whether friendly patrol be liable to be encounter and where message be to be send or the patrol be to report important and comprehensive instruction should be in write but precaution against capture of papers must be take a officer send out a patrol must be certain that he order be understand detailed instruction be as a rule avoid when necessary the time of return be state the patrol leader should be select with care he should have good judgment courage be able to read map make sketch and send clear and concise message in addition to he ordinary equipment he should have a map of the country a watch field glass compass whistle message blank and pencil the leader of a patrol should carefully inspect it before start out and see that each member be in good physical condition have serviceable shoe a full canteen one ration a first-aid packet and that he rifle and ammunition be in good condition he will see that the equipment be arrange so as not to rattle that nothing bright be expose so as to glitter in the sunlight that nothing be take along that will give information to the enemy should any member fall into he hand as for example copy of order map with position of troops marked thereon letter newspaper or collar ornament blanket roll should generally be leave behind in order that the patrol may travel as light as possible the leader then give he patrol information and instruction these embrace instruction from higher authority he detailed plan information of the country and enemy the countersign if any the point where the patrol will assemble if scatter he will see that the man understand the prescribed signal it must always be remember that it make no difference how valuable may be the information that the patrol get it be worthless if not send back in time to be of service herein be where most patrol full this apply particularly to the information obtain by patrol act as a point or flanker of advance rear and flank guard whenever the patrol get any information the leader must think whether the commanding officer would change he plan or issue new order if he have the information if he would the information should be send back at once if the distance be great or the inhabitant be hostile it be well to send two man with the message these man should not travel side by side but as a patrol of two man if the information be very important and the danger of capture be considerable the message should be send by two party each travel by a different route a message from a patrol should always show -lrb- a -rrb- the place from which it be send -lrb- b -rrb- the time it be send -lrb- date hour and minute -rrb- -lrb- c -rrb- to whom it be send -lrb- d -rrb- the message itself -lrb- e -rrb- what the patrol intend do after send the message -lrb- f -rrb- the name of the sender under -lrb- d -rrb- care must be take to separate what have actually be see by the patrol from information receive from other source care must also be take not to exaggerate what be see but to report only the exact fact in they conduct patrol exercise the greatest vigilance to prevent discovery no formal formation be or should be prescribe under the leader 's guidance it move so as to guard against surprise usually with point and flanker to extend the sphere of its observation still smaller patrol -lrb- one or two man -rrb- may be send out for short distance communication with the leader be maintain by signal whatever the formation adopt it should favor the escape of at least one man in case of surprise in patrol of two to five man the commander generally lead in this formation few signal be necessary the man simply regulate they movement by he in question civilian caution be observe not to disclose information that may be of value to the enemy stranger be not allow to precede the patrol patrol lender be authorize to seize telegram and mail matter and to arrest individual report the fact as soon as possible patrol should observe everything for sign of the enemy even apparent trifle may be of great value the finding of a collar ornament show a man 's regiment may enable the chief of staff to determine that the enemy have be reenforce patrol should not travel on the main road if they can observe they and at the same time make the necessary progress by move some distance to the side of the road unless in case of attack or of great personal danger no member of the patrol should fire on hostile troops without order from the patrol leader when send out to gain information patrol should avoid fight unless it be absolutely necessary in order to carry out they order village and inclosure involve danger of surprise be enter with precaution and for brief period only halt be make at point afford good view and the country be study in all direction landmark to the rear be impress on the mind of the man so that the way back can be readily find the leader consult he map and locate himself thereon when a patrol be scatter it reassemble at some place previously select if check in one direction it take another if cut off it return by a detour or force its way through as a last resort it scatter so that at least one man may return with information patrol near they own line should march at a walk unless press by the enemy occasionally it be advisable fur the leader to conceal he patrol and continue the reconnoissance with one or two companion patrol far from they command or in contact with the enemy often remain out overnight in such case they seek a place of concealment proceeding thereto after nightfall or under cover when the enemy be encounter it be very necessary to locate he main force information be particularly desire of he strength whether he have infantry cavalry and artillery the route and direction of he march or the location of he camp and line of outpost dust cloud indicate move body infantry raise a low thick cloud cavalry a high thin cloud artillery and wagon a broken cloud the kind of troops direction of march and approximate strength may thus sometimes be roughly estimate if from some position a body of troops can be see march along in column the exact time in minute and seconds it require for they to pa a certain point should be note together with the formation they be in thus : infantry column of squad three minute and twelve seconds cavalry column of two at a trot one minute and twenty seconds wagon four-mule five minute from this information the strength can be determine by the follow rule : assume that infantry in column of squad occupy half a yard per man cavalry in column of fours 1 yard per man and artillery and wagon in single column 20 yard per gun caisson or wagon a give point would be pass in one minute by about -- 175 infantry 110 cavalry at a walk 200 cavalry at a trot 5 gun caisson or wagon for troops in column of two take one-half of the above estimate patrol should always observe the country march over with a view to make a report on the same the follow information be always of value : road -- direction kind whether dirt gravel macadam etc width whether suitable for column of squad etc border whether fence with stone barb wire rail etc steepness in cross hill and valley where they pass through defile and along command height etc crossroads surround country -- whether generally open and passable for infantry cavalry and artillery or whether broken and impassable due to fence wood crop ravine etc railroad -- single or double track narrow or broad gauge tunnel bridge cut direction station etc bridge -- material wood stone steel etc : length and breadth number and kind of pier or support river -- direction width depth kind of bottom such as mud sand rocky etc : bank steep or gentle open or wooded rapidity of current variation in depth at different time as indicate by driftwood and high-water mark island height in vicinity commanding stream wood -- extent and shape kind of tree free from underbrush or not clearing road swamp ravine etc telegraph line -- number of wire along rond or railroad station etc village -- size kind of house nature of street mean of defense etc hill and ridge -- whether slope be gentle or steep whether top be narrow or wide whether ground be break or smooth wooded or clear whether difficult or easy to cross etc whether command by other hill defile -- they direction length and width whether surround height be passable for infantry and artillery kind of country at each opening of the defile etc ravine ditch etc -- width and depth bank whether passable for infantry cavalry and wagon whether suitable for trench or for movement of troops therein etc in general every soldier should be constantly on the lookout to obtain information that might be of some military value remember that information of the enemy and of the country be worthless unless make know to the proper official in time to be of use every soldier should be able to find he way in a strange country should know how to use a compass should know how to locate the north star should be able to travel across country keep a give direction both by day and by night and by observe landmark he should be able to return to the start point either over the same route or by a more circuitous one this can easily be learn by a little practice it add a great deal to the value of a soldier if he know how to use a map to find he way if he know how to make a rough sketch of the country show the position of road stream wood railroad bridge house village field fence hill etc he have add to he value as a soldier very much indeed because a rough sketch of a country will give more and better information at a glance than can be obtain by read many page of write description patrolling be one of the most important duty a soldier can learn any enlist man who understand thoroughly he duty as a member of a patrol will understand also most of he duty when with advance or rear guard or when on outpost duty patrolling can not be learn merely by read book nor by work indoors thoroughness come only by actually go out in the country and act as a patrol in carry out this idea the follow scheme be recommend : let four or more man and a noncommissioned officer act as a patrol they assemble at a certain time at a convenient point on some country road a officer whom we will call captain a act as the director the noncommissioned officer whom we will call sergeant b act as patrol leader and the other -lrb- private c d e etc -rrb- act as member of sergeant b 's patrol assume that the company -lrb- battalion etc -rrb- have just make camp in this vicinity find that the inhabitant be friendly -lrb- or hostile -rrb- captain a indicate to the rest of the man where the camp be situate and point out where the various sentinel be post -lrb- this in itself afford a opportunity for much discussion and for teach many valuable lesson -rrb- captain a then call up sergeant b and tell he -- -lrb- a -rrb- just what information captain a have of the enemy and also any information of the country or of friendly as part of the patrol go along with captain a as observer -lrb- c -rrb- how far he shall go and what country he shall cover with the patrol -lrb- d -rrb- just what information it be particularly desire he shall obtain -lrb- e -rrb- where he shall send he message and when he shall return example 1 : sergeant b it have just be report to I that a company of hostile infantry be in camp last night at x about 5 mile from here on this road take 5 man and proceed toward x and find out whether the enemy be still there and if not when he leave and where he go send message to I here and return by 8 o'clock this evening example 2 : sergeant b i think i hear the firing of field gun over in that direction a short while ago take 6 man and proceed to that high hill you see over there about 4 mile away send a message to I here when you reach there you may go farther if you then think it advisable but return before daylight i desire particularly to know if there be any hostile troops in this vicinity especially artillery i shall send sergeant x with 3 man to observe the country from that hill you see over there farther to the south he will remain there till dark send message to I here if the company be not here on you return you will find a note for you underneath this rail example 3 : sergeant b this friendly country boy have just report that four hostile cavalryman stop about half a disappear you will reconnoiter in that vicinity until dark this boy will accompany you as a guide i desire particularly to learn the position strength and composition of any hostile troops in this infantry message will reach I here return by 8 o'clock to-night sergeant b then inspect he man and give they they instruction the patrol be then form and move out exactly as it would under actual war condition captain a may halt -lrb- and assemble if desirable -rrb- the patrol at interval in order to discuss the formation use and the movement of any member of the patrol they route use of cover etc with the reason therefor and compare the same with suggest modification of the formation etc after the discussion the patrol be again set in motion captain a may accompany any part of the patrol from private -- with instruction -rrb- captain a must in this case make note of what the message be in either case private -- cease to be a member of the patrol and join captain a as a observer he should discuss be it proper to send a message at this time do sergeant b intend to remain in observation if so how long -lrb- captain a can give such information from time to time concern the hostile patrol as sergeant b might reasonably be suppose to learn in view of he disposition in order that captain a may present natural assumption it be very essential that in he own mind he should at the outset
