company officer may use this method of instruct non-commissioned officer in patrolling advance and rear guard duty outpost and in squad lead in write message in select position for trench and in construct and conceal same this form of instruction be call a tactical walk it be very greatly use by all foreign army exercise along the same general line be conduct for field and staff officer and even general officer and be call tactical ride and strategical ride depend upon they object after some proficiency have be attain as a result of these tactical walk the greatest interest and enthusiasm can be awaken in this work by send out two patrol the same day one to operate against the other each should wear a distinctive uniform the strength of each patrol its start point route to be follow and its order should all be unknown to the other patrol if blank ammunition be use a officer should supervise its issue and carefully inspect to see that no man carry any ball cartridge one umpire should accompany the commander of each party each umpire should be fully inform of the strength order and route of both patrol he must however carefully avoid give suggestion or offer any information to the commander observer in these small maneuver problem be generally in the way and none should be permit to be along these small maneuver may be gradually develop by have one side establish al outpost or fight a delaying action etc it should always be remember that there be no hard and fast rule prescribe how a patrol of three five or any number of man should march the same be equally true of advance guard and apply also to the establishment of outpost it be simply a question of common sense base on military knowledge do not try to remember any diagram in a book think only of what you have be order to do and how best you can handle you man to accomplish you mission and at the same time save the man from any unnecessary hardship never use two or more man to do what one can do just as well and do not let you man get beyond you control in addition to the signal prescribe in the infantry drill regulation the following should be clearly understand by the member of a patrol enemy in sight in small number hold rifle above the head horizontally enemy in force same proceeding raise and lower the rifle several time take cover a downward motion of the hand other signal may be agree upon but they must be familiar to the man complicate signal be avoid signal must be use cautiously so as not to convey information to the enemy section 4 advance guard the advance guard be a detachment of the main body which precede and cover it on the march the primary duty of a advance guard be to insure the safe and uninterrupted march of the main body specifically its duty be : 1 to guard against surprise and furnish information by reconnoiter 2 to push back small party of the enemy and prevent they observe firing upon or delay the main body 3 to check the enemy 's advance in force long enough to permit the main body to prepare for action 4 when the enemy be encounter on the defensive to seize a good position and locate he line care be take not to bring on a general engagement unless the advance guard commander be empower to do so 5 to remove obstacle repair the road and favor in every way the steady march of the column the strength of the advance guard will vary with the proximity of the enemy and character of the country for a regiment it will generally consist of from two company to a battalion for a battalion of one company for a company of from a squad to a platoon the advance guard commander be responsible for the proper performance of the duty with which it be charge and for its conduct and formation the advance guard provide for its security and gain information by throw out to the front and flank smaller body each part must keep in touch with the unit from which it be send out a advance guard be generally divide into a reserve and a support where it consist of less than a battalion the reserve be generally omit the support send forward a advance party which in turn send forward a point in small advance guard the point precede the advance party about 150 yard the advance party the support about 300 yard and the support the main body about 400 yard where advance guard be large enough to require a reserve these distance be increase about one-fourth the reserve follow the support the main body follow the reserve at a distance vary from 500 to 800 yard unless the country to the flank be distinctly visible from the road for a distance of what may be say to be effective rifle fire approximately 1000 yard flanking patrol of two or three man each should be send out from the advance party and when in proximity of the enemy in addition from the support when the nature of the country be such that patrol may move across country without undue effort and fatigue these patrol should march at a distance of from 200 to 300 yard from the flank of the body from which detach for the examination of any object such as a wood building etc examine patrol should be send out from the main body the usual method of protect the flank particularly when the country be at all cut up or difficult be to send out patrol from time to time to some point from which a good outlook can be obtain or which will afford protection to the enemy these patrol remain in observation until the advance guard have pass when they rejoin the nearest subdivision as quickly as possible work they way to that to which they belong during the halt by send out a succession of small patrol in this manner the flank be protect should the advance party become deplete it must be reenforce from the support a battalion act as advance guard would have two company in reserve and two in support the support would send forward as advance party two platoon the advance party in turn send forward as point one squad a company act as advance guard would have no reserve and would send forward as advance party one platoon case may arise when the best means of cover the head and flank of the column will be by a line of skirmisher extend at interval of from 5 to 50 yard as for instance when pass through high corn underbrush etc it must always be remember that the principal duty of the advance guard be to secure the uninterrupted march of the main body if the point be fire upon it should at once deploy and endeavor to advance fight the flanker should assist in this and endeavor to locate the enemy 's flank should there be such resistance that advance be impossible each succeed body should march promptly forward and in turn be place in action with the idea of clear the way for the advance of the main body should this be impossible the commander of the entire body must determine what measure he will take section 5 rear guard a rear guard be a detachment detail to protect the main body from attack in rear in a retreat it check pursuit and enable the main body to increase the distance between it and the enemy and to re-form if disorganize the general formation be that of a advance guard reverse its commander should take advantage of every favorable opportunity to delay the pursuer by obstruct the road or by take up specially favorable position from which to force the enemy to deploy in this latter case care must be take not to become so closely engage as to render withdrawal unnecessarily difficult the position take should be select with reference to ease of withdrawal and ability to bring the enemy under fire at long range section 6 flank guard a flank guard be a detachment detail to cover the flank of a column march past or across the front of a enemy it may be place in position to protect the passage or it may be so march as to cover the passage the object of the flank guard be to hold the enemy in check long enough to enable the main body to pass or like the advance guard to enable the main body to deploy like all other detachment it should be no larger than be necessary and should not be detail except when its protection be require when a flank guard consist of a regiment or less its distance from the main body should not exceed a mile and a half practicable communication must exist between it and the main body the flank guard be march as a separate command that be with advance or rear guard or both as circumstance demand and with patrolling on the expose flank section 7 outpost troops not on the march provide for they security by outpost the general duty of a outpost be reconnoissance observation and resistance the specific duty be : 1 to protect the main body so that the troops may rest undisturbed 2 in case of attack to check the enemy long enough to enable the main body to make the necessary disposition during a advance the outpost be usually detail from the advance guard during the retreat the outpost for the night usually form the rear guard the next day if the command remain in bivouac the new outpost generally go on duty at daybreak the vigilance of outpost troops must be unceasing but they should avoid bring on combat or unnecessarily alarming the command firing disturb the rest of troops and if frequently indulge in cease to be a warning no trumpet signal except to arm or to horse be sound and all unnecessary noise must be avoid as a rule a outpost will not exceed one-sixth the strength of a command for a single company a few sentinel and patrol will suffice for a larger command a more elaborate system must be devise the troops compose the outpost be generally divide into a reserve and several support at a proper distance in front of the camp of the main body a line which offer a good defensive position be select this be call the line of resistance and should he so located that a advance enemy will be hold in check beyond effective rifle range in case of a small force artillery range in case of a large force of the main body until the latter can deploy the reserve be station at some point in rear of this line where it can be move quickly to reinforce any point as need the line of resistance be divide into section the limit of each of which be clearly define a support be assign to each section which be number from right to leave and occupy a position on or near the line have special regard to cover avenue of approach the position occupy should always be intrench the reserve and support proceed to they respective position by the shortest route provide for they own protection by send out cover detachment generally speak about one-half the infantry of the advance guard should be in the support as each support arrive at its position it send out observation group vary in size from four man to a platoon to watch the country in the direction of the enemy these group be call outguard for convenience they be classify as picket sentry squad and cossack post and should be sufficient in number to cover the front of the section occupy by the support and connect with the neighbor support a picket be a group consist of two or more squad ordinarily not exceed half a company post in the line of outpost to cover a give sector it furnish patrol and one or more sentinel sentry squad or cossack post for observation picket be place at the more important point in the line of outguard such as road fork the strength of each depend upon the number of small group require to observe properly its sector a sentry squad be a squad -lrb- eight man -rrb- post in observation at a indicated point it post a double sentinel in observation the remain man rest near by and furnish the relief of sentinel in some case it may be require to furnish a patrol a cossack post consist of four man it be a observation group similar to a sentry squad but employ a single sentinel as a rule not more than one-third of the support should be on outguard duty as soon as they be send out to they postion the support commander select a defensive position on the line of resistance give instruction for intrench same establish a sentinel to watch for and transmit signal from outguard send out patrol to reconnoiter the country to the front of he section and if on the flank of the line the flank and then proceed to make a careful reconnoissance of the section assign he rectify the position of outguard if necessary see that they understand they instruction in case of attack or when stranger approach they post and point out they line of retreat in case they be compel to fall back on the support when the outguard be establish the member of the support may stack arm and remove equipment except cartridge belt no fire will be build or smoking permit unless specially authorize or no loud talking or other noise all patrolling to the front will be do as a rule from the support the support commander should locate the position of the adjacent support und make arrangement with the commander for the joint defense of the line of resistance at night all road and trail should be carefully cover and the country to the front and between adjacent outguard well patrol the line occupy by the outguard be call the line of observation outguard move to they position provide for they own protection and so we to conceal the movement from the enemy these position be intrench and be number from right to leave in each support the duty of the outguard be to observe the enemy to guard the outpost from surprise and to make a preliminary resistance to the enemy 's advance the strength of the outguard will vary accord to its object when a important road which at night will afford a line of advance or a bridge be to be cover or when several post be establish from a outguard it should be of considerable strength two squad or a platoon when mere observation and alarm be all that be require four man will suffice a squall be a good unit to use as a outguard this will allow one double sentry post of three relief and one man in addition to the commander who may be use for messenger service the outguard should be carefully conceal the utmost quiet should be observe and there should be no cooking or smoking the interval between outguard will depend upon the situation and the terrain the line of observation be not necessarily continuous but all avenue of approach must be carefully guard the distance of the outguard from the support likewise be govern by the terrain but in general may be say to be from 300 to 400 yard in thick country or at night outguard patrol along the line of observation between post communication between outguard and the support be by signal and messenger in special case by wire member of the outguard retain possession of they weapon and do not remove they equipment sentinel from the outguard be post so as to avoid observation but so that they may have a clear lookout and be able to see if possible by day the sentinel of the adjacent outguard double sentinel be always post near enough to each other to communicate easily in ordinary voice sentinel be generally on post two hour out of six for every sentinel and every patrol there should be three relief and outguard should be of a strength sufficient to allow this the position of a sentinel should be select with reference to observation it may be advantageous to place a sentinel in a tree sentinel furnish by cossack post or sentry squad be keep near they group those furnish by they picket may be keep as far sa 100 yard away relief visit patrol and inspect officer approach sentinel from the rear a sentinel on the line of observation should always have the follow instruction : the name of village stream and prominent feature in sight and where the road lead the number -lrb- if any -rrb- of he post and the number of he and of the adjoining outguard the position of the support the line of retreat to be follow if the outguard be compel to fall back the position of advance detachment and whether friendly patrol be operate in front to watch to the front and flank without intermission and devote special attention to unusual or suspicious occurrence if he see indication of the enemy to at once notify he immediate superior in case of imminent danger or when a attack be make to give the alarm by firing rapidly by day to pass in or out officer noncommissioned officer and detachment recognize as part of the outpost and officer know to have authority to do so to detain all other and notify the outguard commander at night when person approach he post to come to a ready halt they and notify the outguard commander the latter challenge ascertain they identity and act accordingly when individual fail to halt or otherwise disobey to fire upon they after a second warning or sooner if they attempt to attack or escape to require deserter to lay down they arm and remain until a patrol be send out to bring they in to order deserter pursue by the enemy to drop they arm and to give a alarm if they fail to obey they be fire upon to require bearer of flag of truce and they escort to halt and to face outward to permit they to hold no conversation and to see that they be then blindfold and dispose of in accordance with instruction from the support commander if they fall to obey to fire upon they at night to remain practically stationary move about for purpose of observation only not to sit or lie down unless authorize to do so in the daytime to make use of natural or artificial cover and assume such position as to give he the best field of view to inform pass patrol of what he have see to carry he weapon habitually load and lock and at will outpost patrol be divide into those which operate beyond the line and those whose duty lie principally within the line the former call reconnoitering patrol scout in the direction of the enemy the latter call visit patrol maintain communication between the part of the outpost and supervise the performance of duty on the line of observation reconnoissance should be continuous though scout and detachment of cavalry remain in contact with the enemy or at least push forward to a considerable distance more detailed reconnoissance by infantry patrol in the foreground must not be neglect reconnoitering patrol be compose of at least two man and a skillful leader who in important case would be a officer they obtain information ascertain the presence of the enemy or discover he approach all patrol when they cross the line of observation inform the nearest sentinel of the direction in which they be to advance on they return they similarly report what they have see of the enemy signal be agree upon so that they can be recognize when return any ground near the line of observation which might afford cover for troops or for scout or spy and the approach to which can not be observe by sentinel be search frequently by patrol definite information concern the enemy be report at once patrol fire only in self-defense or to give the alarm support on the flank of a outpost position patrol the country on the expose flank visit patrol and relief should not march in the open and thereby expose the position of sentinel during a march in the vicinity of the enemy when halt be make special measure for protection be take when the halt be for a short period less than half a hour the advance party and support remain at ease the point and flanker move to position from which they can obtain a good lookout and additional patrol may be send out from advance party and support where the halt be for a period exceed half a hour a march outpost should be form with a advance guard consist of a battalion 2 company in the reserve 2 in the support the latter have as advance party one-half a company a typical march outpost would be form as follow : the advance party would send one platoon four or five hundred yard to the right as outguard no 1 the remain platoon constitute outguard no 2 a platoon from the head of the support would be send a similar distance to the leave as outguard no 3 the balance of the support would constitute the support of the march outpost the reserve of the advance guard act as reserve on signal be give to resume the march the various unit would close in and as soon as the advance party have assemble the march would be take up section 8 rifle trench soldier should remember that only by act vigorously on the offensive can a army hope to gain the victory the defensive may delay or stop the enemy but it can never destroy he troops dig because they be force to halt they do not halt to dig trench will frequently be construct without be use and soldier must expect this as a feature of campaigning and accept cheerfully what at time may appear as unnecessary labor when intrench under fire cover be first secure in the lie position each man scoop out a depression for he body and throw the earth to the front in this position no excavation can be conveniently make for the leg but if time permit the original excavation be enlarged and deepen until it be possible to assume a sit position with the leg cross and the shoulder to the parapet in such a position a man present a smaller target to shrapnel bullet than in the lie trench and can fire more comfortably and with less exposure than in the kneel trench from the sit position the excavation may be continue until a standing trench be secure the accompany plate show some of the more common form of trench in profile figure 1 be the simplest form of stand trench figure 2 show the same trench deepen in rear so as to allow man to walk along in the rear -lrb- deeper -rrb- portion of the trench without expose they head above the parapet figure 3 show a cover and firing trench with a chamber in which man can find shelter when under heavy artillery fire when the excavate earth be easily remove figure 4 show a good profile the enemy 's infantry as well as he artillery will generally have great difficulty in see this type of trench the mound or bank of earth throw up for shelter in front of a trench be call the parapet it should be at least 30 inch thick on top and the front should slope gradually as show in the plate so that shell will tend to glance from it rather than penetrate and explode the top should be cover with sod grass or leave so as to hide the newly turn earth which could be easily see and aim at by the enemy there should be no rock loose stone or pebble on top which might be strike by the bullet splinter and fly thus add greatly to the number of dangerous projectile and often deflect bullet downward into the trench a stone wall be a very dangerous thing to be behind in a fight the portion of the ground in rear of the parapet and between the parapet and the trench not cover by the parapet be to rest the elbow on when firing the rifle be rest on top of the parapet to obtain head cover in a trench fill a gunny sack or other bag with sand or soil and place it on top of the parapet aim around the right-hand side of it or dig a small lateral trench in the parapet large enough to hold the rifle roof it over with board small log or brush and heap dirt on top aim through the small trench or result loophole figure 5 show the plan of a section of a rifle trench -lrb- 7 -rrb- between the portion occupy by each squad there be often place a mound of earth as high as the top of the parapet and project back into the trench this be call a traverse and protect the occupant of the trench from fire from a flank bullet from this direction hit a traverse instead of fly down into the trench and wound several man -lrb- footnote 7 : the traverse should be at least 6 foot wide instead of 3 foot as show in figure 5 -rrb- trench be seldom continuous but be make in section place at the most advantageous point as show in figure 6 a company or battalion may occupy a single section the firing trench have cover trench in rear of they where the support can rest undisturbed by the hostile fire until they be need in the firing trench to repel a serious assault or to take part in a counter attack passage consist of deep communicate trench facilitate passage from the cover trench to the firing trench when under fire these communicate trench be usually zigzag or traverse to prevent they be sweep by hostile fire when troops be likely to remain in trench for a considerable time drainage should be arrange for and latrine and dress station should be construct in trench water should be bring into the trench and hole excavate in the front wall of the trench for extra ammunition in digging trench man usually work in relief one relief digging while the other rest the proportion of shoveler to pick man be about 3 to 1 if a plow can be obtain to turn the sod it will greatly facilitate the initial work of digging -lrb- illustration : plate v -rrb- chapter vii march and camp section 1 breaking camp and preparation for a march the evening before the march when a command learn that it be to make a march on the follow day presumably start early in the morning certain detail should be attend to the evening before all man should fill they canteen as there will probably be no time for this in the morning the mess sergeant should find out whether lunch or the reserve ration will be carry on the march and should attend to these detail in the evening in order that the issue can be make promptly in the morning the commander of the guard should be give a memorandum as to what time to awaken the cook and where they tent be the member of the guard who do this should awaken they without noise so as not to disturb the rest of the remainder of the command the cook should be instruct as to what time breakfast be to be serve and what time to awaken the first sergeant the cook or cook 's police must cut and split all firewood for the morning before 9 p m there must be no chop talking or rattle of pan before reveille which will disturb the rest of the command this apply to every morning in camp the morning of the march cook arise when call by the guard and start the preparation of breakfast without noise the first sergeant be usually awaken by one of the cook about half a hour before reveille in order that he may complete he toilet and breakfast early and be able to devote all he time to supervise the detail of the morning 's work if the officer desire to be awaken before reveille they will notify the first sergeant accordingly at first call the man turn out perform they toilet strike they shelter tent -lrb- unless it have be direct to await the sound of the general for this -rrb- and make up they pack at the sound of assembly immediately after reveille each man must be in he proper place in rank this assembly be under arm the first sergeant start to call the roll or command report at the last note of assembly arm be stack before the company be dismiss breakfast be serve to the company immediately after roll call immediately after breakfast each man will wash he mess kit in the hot water provide for that purpose at the kitchen and will at once pack the mess kit in he haversack the cook will provide hot water for wash mess kit at the same time that breakfast be serve immediately after breakfast the company proceed to the work of break camp and packing in accordance with a prearranged system similar to the following : one squad assist the cook in pack the kitchen one squad strike and fold the officer ' tent and bring they to the kitchen one squad fill in the sink the sink should not be fill in earlier than be absolutely necessary one squad police the camp within the company police limit one squad be available for possible detail from regimental headquarters officer and first sergeant supervise the work a permanent assignment of squad to these duty lighten the labor and decrease the time necessary for break camp after the breaking of camp the entire company be use to police camp man should not start from camp thirsty but should drink all the water they want immediately after breakfast all canteen should be fill before march one man in each squad be detail to fill the canteen for he squad at assembly for the march the man fall in in rear or the stack fully equip for march section 2 march the principal work of troops in the field consist of march battle take place only at indefinite interval but march be of daily occurrence it be only by good march that troops can arrive at a give point at a give time and in good condition for battle the rate of march depend greatly upon the condition of the road and the weather but the average rate for infantry be about 2-1\/2 mile per hour this allow for a rest of 10 minute each hour the total distance march in a day depend not only on the rate of march but upon the size of the command large command often cover only about 10 mile a day while small command easily cover double that distance in order to make the march with the greatest comfort and the least danger it be necessary that each unit be keep well in hand each man be permit and encourage to make himself as comfortable as possible at all time except only that he must not interfere with the comfort of other or with the march of the column infantry generally march in column of squad but on narrow road or trail column of two or file be use the route step be habitually use when silence be not require in large command in order that the column be keep in hand it be very necessary that each man keep he place in rank and follow he file leader at the prescribe distance this be one of the best test for determine the discipline and efficiency of troops the equipment should be carefully adjust before start out and any part that be not comfortable should be rearrange at the first opportunity the rifle be carry at will except that the muzzle must be point up so as not to interfere with the other man under no circumstance will any man leave the rank without permission from he company or higher commander if the absence be to be for more than a short while he must be give a pass show he name rank and organization and the reason he be permit to be absent if sick it be better to wait by the roadside at some comfortable place for the arrival of the surgeon or the ambulance in any case the soldier keep he rifle and equipment with he if possible soldier absent from they organization without a pass will be arrest and return to they command for punishment march in hot weather be particularly try green leaf or a damp cloth carry in the hat lessen the chance of sunstroke the hat should have ventilator and when not expose to the direct ray of the sun it should be remove from the head it be well to keep the clothing about the neck and throat open and sometimes to turn up the shirt sleeve so as to leave the wrist free the canteen should always be fill before start out use the water very sparingly none at all should be drunk during the first three or four hour of the march after that take only a few mouthful at a time and wash out the mouth and throat except possibly in very hot weather one canteen of water should last for the entire day 's march excessive water drinking on the march will play a man out very quickly old soldier never drink when march a small pebble carry in the mouth keep it moist and therefore reduce thirst or a small piece of chocolate may occasionally be eat smoking be very depressing during a march canteen will not be refill on the march without authority from a officer as the clearest water whether from a well spring or run stream may be very impure and the source of many camp disease if canteen be to be refill it should be do by order and a detail be generally make for this purpose enter upon private property without permission or steal fruit etc from garden and orchard be a serious military offense as well as a violation of the civil law when a cook meal be carry it should not be eat until the proper time a command ordinarily march for 50 minute and halt for 10 minute the first halt in a day 's march be for about 15 minute be make after about 30 minute ' march and be for the express purpose of allow the man to relieve themselves man who wish to do this should attend to it at once and not wait until the command be almost ready to march again at every halt get all the rest possible and do not spend the time wander around or stand about only green recruit do this if the ground be dry stretch out at full length remove the pack or blanket roll and belt and get in as comfortable position as possible the next best way be to sit down with a good back rest against a tree or a fence or some other object never sit down or lie down however on wet or damp ground sit on you pack or blanket roll or on anything else that be dry at a halt it be very refreshing to adjust the underclothing section 3 make camp on reach the camp site the man should be allow to fall out and rest as soon as the arm have be stack and the shelter tent pitch if the blanket roll have be carry on the wagon then the location of the front pole of the shelter tent should be mark before they be allow to fall out the man will not be allow to relieve themselves until sink be dig temporary sink may be dig with intrenching tool if carry a guard should be place over the water supply at once as soon as the shelter tent be pitch the company proceed to the remainder of the camp work in accordance with a permanent assignment similar to the following : one squad help arrange the kitchen one squad pitch the officer ' tent one squad dig the sink one squad procure wood and water one squad be hold available for detail from regimental headquarters the officer and first sergeant supervise the work the sink be locate by the commanding officer the detail to dig they should wait until inform of the location a officer should inspect the sink as soon as the detail report it as complete after the camp have be put in order the first sergeant make the detail from roster for kitchen police and noncommissioned officer in charge of quarter for the next day and for such guard as may be order for that day the detail call for by regimental headquarters for pitch the headquarters camp for the quartermaster etc should be report to the adjutant without delay the cook pitch they tent at that end of the company street nearest the kitchen space must be leave for this tent if the cook be not in rank when the company pitch tent unless lunch have be carry or cook during the march the cook should get to work on a hot meal as soon as possible the kitchen police report at the kitchen as soon as they tent be pitch wood and water will be require at once officer should avoid keep the man unnecessarily under arm or on they foot after a hard day 's march when the detail of make camp have be complete all man should at once care for they rifle and foot -lrb- for detail as to the care of the rifle see chapter ii section 1 for the care of the foot see chapter iv -rrb- section 4 camp service and duty in camp reveille be precede by first call and a march play by the band or field music and be follow immediately by assembly if there be a reveille gun it be fire at the first note of the march and be the signal for all to arise the roll be call at the last note of assembly after reveille at this formation man should fall in in the proper uniform -- rifle and belt service hat olive-drab flannel shirt service breeches leggings and shoe the regimental commander may prescribe that coat be to be worn and will prescribe the exact uniform for all drill parade and other formation as well as for man go on pass immediately after reveille roll call the sergeant next in rank to the first sergeant take command of the company and deploy it for a general police of the camp within the limit assign to the company man pick up all scrap of paper and rubbish of all kind deposit it in the company incinerator or place designate for the purpose the police limit of each company be usually designate as extend from head to rear of camp within the space occupy by the company street include the ground occupy by the tent of the company no unassigned space be leave between company immediately after breakfast man police they tent and raise wall of same if the day be fair all bedding should be spread on the tent for several hour ' airing at sick call all man who be sick fall in and be march to the regimental infirmary under charge of the noncommissioned officer in charge of quarter the noncommissioned officer take with he the company sick report previously fill in and sign by the company commander the surgeon examine all those report and indicate they status on the sick report this status may be duty -lrb- available for all duty -rrb- quarter -lrb- patient to remain in tent or company street -rrb- and hospital -lrb- patient to be send to the hospital -rrb- the noncommissioned officer then return to the company with all the man not marked hospital and hand the sick report to the first sergeant at drill call the company prepare for drill and fall in so that it will be completely form at assembly which be usually sound 10 minute after drill call all man be require to attend drill except those excuse by sick report and those specially excuse from headquarters the excuse list should include in each company only the mess sergeant the two cook one kitchen police and man on regimental guard during drill hour the guard to be excuse should be limit to a small patrol to guard against fire and thief in camp if the bedding have be air it should be take in immediately after drill and place in the tent neatly fold some time during the morning at a time designate by he the company commander inspect the entire company camp at this inspection the entire street should be police kitchen in order and tent police as follow : in permanent camp when pyramidal conical or wall tent be use : bedding fold neatly and place on the head of the cot -lrb- if bed sack be use they will be fold in three fold and the bedding place on top -rrb- hat on top of the bedding shoe under foot of cot surplus kit bag at side of squad leader 's cot equipment suspend neatly from a frame arrange around the tent pole rifle in rack construct around the tent pole in shelter-tent camp : bedding neatly fold and place at rear of tent poncho underneath equipment arrange on the bedding rifle lay on bedding except when use as tent pole the regimental commander prescribe the exact scheme to be follow in the police of tent should there be no parade retreat roll call be hold at the same hour this roll call be under arm and be supervise by a officer of the company after the roll call and at the sound of retreat the officer bring the company to parade rest and keep it in this position during the sound of this call at the first note of the national anthem -lrb- the star-spangled banner -rrb- or to the color the company be bring to attention and so stand until the end of the play the officer then report the result of the roll call to the adjutant or officer of the day return to the company inspect the arm and dismiss it at the sound of call to quarter all man will repair to they company street after tap have sound all talk must cease and all light must be extinguish and so remain until first call for reveille in camp all enlist man be prohibit from cross the officer ' street or from visit officer ' tent unless actually engage in some duty require they to do so or send for by a officer man be not allow to leave camp without a pass sign by the company commander and countersign by the regimental adjutant the first sergeant be sometimes allow to give man permission to leave camp from retreat to tap the noncommissioned officer in charge of quarter detail for 24 hour go on duty each day at reveille he be responsible that the grounds around the company be keep in proper police that no loud noise disturbance or disorder occur in the company street that man confine to the company street do not leave the same without proper authority he report man who be sick to the surgeon he may be require to report all other detail call for he accompany the captain in he daily inspection of the company he will not leave the company street during he tour of duty except as provide above one or two private be detailed daily as kitchen police they go on duty at reveille it be they duty to assist the cook in the kitchen they assist in the preparation of meal wait on the table wash dish procure water and wood chop firewood and keep the kitchen mess tent and surround ground police they be under the order of the mess sergeant and the cook rifle need careful attention in camp they should be clean and oil daily preferably just before retreat or parade it be advisable for each man to have a canvas cover to keep off the dust and dampness in a shelter-tent camp tie the rifle muzzle up to the pole of the tent place a chip of wood under the butt plate and a oily rag over -lrb- never inside -rrb- the muzzle wet shoe should be fill with oats or dry sand and set in a cool place to dry never dry they by a fire uniform need special care as camp service be very hard on they in a permanent camp every man should have two pair of breeches the coat will seldom be worn except at parade or retreat one pair of breeches and the coat should be keep neat clean and press for use on ceremony inspection and when go on pass woolen uniform may be clean and free from spot by rub with a flannel rag saturate with gasoline cotton uniform may be wash with water soap and a scrub brush wring out and stretch properly crease on a flat wood surface in the sun to dry leggings can be similarly wash hat should be clean with gasoline and dampen and iron to restore they shape enlist man should be very careful to observe all the sanitary regulation of the camp fly be the greatest spreader of camp disease all fecal matter and food should be carefully guard from they in camp extreme precaution be take to screen the sink and kitchen from fly and all enlist man should cooperate in the effort to make these precaution successful one fly carry germ on he foot from the sink to the food can start a serious and fatal epidemic in a camp defecate on the ground in the vicinity of camp or urinating in camp be extremely dangerous to the health of the command and be serious military offens at night a urinal can be provide in each company street in a permanent camp cot or bed sack be usually provide for the man to sleep on in a shelter tent camp bed should be make of hay grass leave pine or spruce bough or pine needle on top of which the poncho and blanket be spread thus soften the ground and keep the sleeper away from the cold and dampness neglect to prepare the bed when sleep without cot or bed sack mean a loss of sleep and may lead to cold bowel disorder and rheumatism in wet weather tent should be ditch and in windy or cold weather dirt may be bank around they a place for wash the person and clothes should be arrange for in each company street and the waste water disposed of by means of drainage or rock-filled pit in dry weather the street in camp should frequently be sprinkle with water to keep down the dust this be specially necessary around the kitchen chapter viii target practice section 1 preliminary training in marksmanship effective rifle fire be generally what count most in battle to have effective rifle fire the man on the firing line must be able to hit what they be order to shoot at there be no man who can not be teach how to shoot it be not necessary or even desirable to begin instruction by firing on a rifle range a perfectly green recruit who have never fire a rifle may be make into a good shot by a little instruction and some preliminary drill and exercise before a man go on the range to fire it be absolutely necessary that he should know -- 1 how to set the rear sight 2 how to sight or aim 3 how to squeeze the trigger 4 how to hold the rifle in all position if he do not know these thing it be worse than useless for he to fire he will not improve the more he shoot the worse he will shoot and it will become more difficult to teach he section 2 sight adjustment man must be able to adjust they sight correctly and quickly a error in adjustment so small that one can scarcely see it on the sight leaf be sufficient to cause a miss at a enemy at 500 yard and over notice you rear sight when the leaf be lay down the battle sight appear on top this sight be set for 547 yard and be not adjustable when the leaf be raise four sight come into view the extreme range sight for 2850 yard at the top of the leaf be seldom use the open sight at the upper edge of the drift slide be adjustable from 1400 to 2750 yard to set it the upper edge of the slide be make to correspond with the range reading on the leaf and the slide be then clamp with the slide screw this sight also be seldom use the open sight at the bottom of the triangular opening in the drift slide be adjustable from 100 to 2450 yard to set it the index line at the lower corner of the triangle be set opposite the range graduation on the leaf and the slide clamp this and the peep sight just below it be the sight most commonly use to set the peep sight the index line on either side of the peephole be set opposite the range desire and the slide clamp notice the scale for the various range on either side of the face of the leaf the odd-numbered hundred of yard be on the right and the even on the leave the line below the number be the index line for that range thus to set the sight for 500 yard the index line of the slide be bring in exact line with the line on the leaf below the figure 5 and the slide clamp to set for 550 yard the index line of the slide be set half way between the index line on the leaf below the figure 5 on the right side and the figure 6 on the left side look at you sight carefully when set it and take great pain to get it exact a error in set the width of one of the line on the leaf will cause a error of about 8 inch in where you bullet will strike at 500 yard the wind gauge be adjust by means of the windage screw at the right front end of the base of the sight each graduation on the wind-gauge scale be call a point for convenience in adjust the line of each third point on the scale be longer than the other if you turn the windage screw so that the movable base move to the right you be take right windage which will cause you rifle to shoot more to the right it be seldom that a rifle will shoot correctly to the point aim at at a give range with the sight adjust exactly to the scale graduation for that range if you sight be not correctly adjust for you shooting and you wish to move it slightly to make it correct remember to move it in the direction you wish you shot to hit if you wish to shoot higher raise you sight if to the right move the wind gauge to the right always move you sight the correct amount in accordance with the follow table : section 3 table of sight correction _ showing_to_what_extent_the_point_of_impact_is_moved_by_a_change _ _ of_25_yards_in_elevation_or_1_point_in_windage _ correction correction by a change by a change range in elevation in windage of 25 yard of 1 point -------- -------------- ------------- _ yard _ _ inch of impact 4 inch for every 100 yard of range copy this table and take it to the range with you example of sight adjustment : suppose you be firing at 500 yard the first two or three shot show you that you shot be hit about a foot below and a foot to the right of the center of the bull 's - eye from the above table you will see that if you will raise you sight 50 yard and move the wind gauge half a point to the leave the rifle will be sight so that if you aim correctly the bullet will hit well inside the bull 's eye section 4 aim open sight : always align you sight with the front sight squarely in the middle of the u or notch of the rear sight and the top of the front sight even with the upper corner of the u -lrb- see fig 1 -rrb- all the sight on the rifle except the peep sight be open sight peep sight : always center the tip of the front sight in the center of the peephole when aim with this sight -lrb- see fig 2 -rrb- -lrb- illustration : figure 1 -rrb- always aim below the bull 's - eye never let you front sight appear to touch the bull 's - eye in aim try to see the same amount of white target between the top of the front sight and the bottom of the bull 's - eye each time the eye must be focus on the bull 's - eye or mark and not on the front or rear sight look at figure 1 and 2 until you eye retain the memory of they then try to duplicate the picture every time you aim aim consistently always the same never change you aim change you sight adjustment if you shot be not hit in the right place section 5 battle sight the battle sight be the open sight see when the leaf be lay flat it be adjust for a range of 547 yard it be intend to be use in battle when you get nearer to the enemy than 600 yard always aim at the belt of a standing enemy or just below he if he be kneel sit or lie on the target range this sight be use for rapid fire with it the rifle shoot about 2 foot high at range between 200 and 400 yard so you must aim below the figure on the target d find out in four instruction practice just how much you must aim below to hit the figure section 6 trigger squeeze use the first joint of the fore finger to squeeze the trigger it be the most sensitive and best control portion of the body as you place the rifle to you shoulder squeeze the trigger so as to pull it back about one-eighth of a inch thus take up the safety portion or slack of the pull then contract the trigger finger gradually slowly and steadily increase the pressure on the trigger while the aim be be perfect continue the gradual increase of pressure so that when the aim have become exact the additional pressure require to release the point of the sear can be give almost insensibly and without cause any deflection of the rifle put absolutely all you mind and will power into hold the rifle steady and squeeze the trigger off without disturb the aim practice squeeze the trigger in this way every time you have you rifle in you hand until you can surely and quickly do it without a suspicion of a jerk -lrb- illustration : figure 2 -rrb- by practice the soldier become familiar with the trigger squeeze of he rifle and know this he be able to judge at any time within limit what additional pressure be require for its discharge by constant repetition of this exercise he should be able finally to squeeze the trigger to a certain point beyond which the slightest movement will release the sear have squeeze the trigger to this point the aim be correct and when true the additional pressure be apply and the discharge follow and the bullet fly true to the mark section 7 firing position when in rank at close order the position be those describe in the infantry drill regulation when in extend order or when firing alone these position may be modify somewhat to better suit the individual the follow remark on the various position be offer as suggestion whereby steady position may be learn by the soldier standing position : face the target then execute right half face plant the foot about 12 inch apart as you raise the ride to the shoulder lean very slightly backward just enough to preserve the perfect balance on both foot which the raising of the rifle have somewhat disturb do not lean far back and do not lean forward at all if you body be out of balance it will be under strain and you will tremble the right elbow should be at about the height of the shoulder the left hand should grasp well around the stock and handguard in front of the rear sight and the left elbow should be almost directly under the rifle the right hand should do more than half the work of hold the rifle up and against the shoulder the left hand only steadying and guide the piece do not try to meet the recoil let the whole body move back with it do not be afraid to press the jaw hard against the stock this steady the position and the head go back with the recoil and insure that you face be not hurt kneel position : assume the position very much as describe in the infantry drill regulation sit on the right heel the right knee should point directly to the right that be along the firing line the point of the left elbow should rest over the left knee there be a flat place under the elbow which fit a flat place on the knee and make a solid rest lean the body well forward this position be uncomfortable until practice when it quickly cease to be uncomfortable sit position : sit down half face to the right foot from 6 to 8 inch apart knee bent right knee slightly higher than the left left leg point toward the target rest both elbow on the knee hand grasp the piece the same as in the prone position this be a very steady position particularly if hole can be find or make in the ground for the heel prone position and use of the gun sling : to adjust the sling for firing unhook the straight strap of the sling and let it out as far as it will go adjust the loop so that when stretch along the bottom of the stock its rear end -lrb- bight -rrb- come about opposite the comb of the stock a small man need a longer loop than a tall man lie down face at a angle of about 60 ° to the right of the direction of the target spread the leg as wide apart as they will go with comfort thrust the left arm through between the rifle and the sling and then back through the loop of the sling secure the loop by means of the keeper around the upper left arm as high up as it will go pass the hand under and then over the sling from the left side and grasp the stock and handguard just in rear of the lower band raise the right elbow off the ground roll slightly over on the left side place the butt to the shoulder and roll back into position clamp the rifle hard and steady in the firing position the rifle should rest deep down in the palm of the left hand with finger almost around the handguard shift the left palm a little to the right or leave until the rifle stand perfectly upright -lrb- no cant -rrb- without effort the left elbow should rest on the ground directly under the rifle and right elbow on the ground about 5 inch to the right of a point directly under the stock in this position the loop of the sling start at the lower band pass to the right of the left wrist and thence around the left upper arm the loop should be so tight that about 50 pound tension be place on it when the position be assume this position be uncomfortable until practice when it quickly cease to be uncomfortable it will be steadier if small hole can be find or dig in the ground for the elbow in this position the sling bind the left forearm to the rifle and to the ground so that it form a dead rest for the rifle with a universal joint the wrist at its upper end also the rifle be so bind to the shoulder that the recoil be not feel at all this be the steadiest of all firing position the gun sling can also be use in this manner with advantage in the other position section 8 call the shot it be evident that the sight should be so adjust at each range that the rifle will hit where you aim in order to determine that the sight be so adjust it be necessary that you shall know each time just where you be aim on the target at the instant you rifle be discharge if you know this and you rifle hit this point you rifle be correctly sight if you shot do not hit near this point you should change you sight adjustment in accordance with the table of sight correction in section 3 no man can hold absolutely steady the rifle tremble slightly and the sight seem to wobble and move over the target you try to squeeze off the last ounce of the trigger squeeze just as the sight move to the desire alignment under the bull 's - eye at this instant just before the recoil blot out a view of the sight and target you should catch with you eye a picture as it be of just where on the target you sight be align and call to yourself or to the coach this point this point be where you shot should strike if you sight be correctly adjust and if you have squeeze the trigger without disturbing you aim until a man can call he shot he be not a good shot for he can never tell if he rifle be sight right or not or if a certain shot be a good one or only the result of luck section 9 coordination good marksmanship consist in learn thoroughly the detail of -- hold the rifle in the various position aim squeeze the trigger call the shot adjust the sight and when these have be master in detail then the coordination of they in the act of firing this coordination consist in put absolutely all of one 's will power into a effort to hold the rifle steadily especially in get it to steady down when the aim be perfect in get the trigger squeeze off easily at the instant the rifle be steadiest and the aim perfect in call the shot at this instant and if the shot do not hit near the point call then in adjust the sight the correct amount so that the rifle will be sight to hit where you aim section 10 advice to rifleman before go to the range clean the rifle carefully remove every trace of oil from the bear this can best be do with a rag saturate with gasoline put a light coat of oil on the bolt and cam blacken the front and rear sight with smoke from a burning candle or camphor or with liquid sight black look through the bear and see that there be no obstruction in it keep the rifle off the ground the stock may absorb dampness the sight may be injure or the muzzle fill with dirt watch you hold carefully and be sure to know where the line of sight be at discharge it be only in this way that the habit of call shot which be essential to good shooting can be acquire study the condition adjust the sling and set the sight before go to the firing point look at the sight adjustment before each shot and see that it have not change if sure of you hold and if the hit be not as call determine and make full correction in elevation and windage to put the next shot in the bull 's - eye keep a write record of the weather condition and the corresponding elevation and windage for each day 's firing less elevation will generally be require on hot day on wet day in a bright sunlight with a 6 o'clock wind or with a cold barrel more elevation will generally be require on cold day on very dry day with a 12 o'clock wind with a hot barrel in a dull or cloudy light the upper band should not be tight enough to bind the barrel do not put a cartridge into the chamber until ready to fire do not place cartridge in the sun they will get hot and shoot high do not rub the eye -- especially the sighting eye in cold weather warm the trigger hand before shooting after shoot clean the rifle carefully and then oil it to prevent rust have a strong clean cloth that will not tear and jam properly cut to size for use in cleaning always clean the rifle from the breech use a brass cleaning rod when available a injury to the rifle at the muzzle cause the piece to shoot very irregularly regular physical exercise take systematically will cause a marked improvement in shooting frequent practice of the position and aim drill be of the greatest help in prepare for shooting on the range rapid firing : success be rapid firing depend upon catch a quick and accurate aim hold the piece firmly and evenly and in squeeze the trigger without a jerk in order to give as much time as possible for aim accurately the soldier must practice take position load with the clip and work the bolt so that no time will be lose in these operation with constant practice all these movement may be make quickly and without false motion when the bolt handle be raise it must be do with enough force to start the shell from the chamber and when the bolt be pull back it must be with sufficient force to throw the empty shell well away from the chamber and far enough to engage the next cartridge in load use force enough to load each cartridge with one motion the aim must be catch quickly and once catch must be hold and the trigger squeeze steadily rapid firing as far as hold aim and squeeze the trigger be concern should be do with all the precision of slow fire the gain in time should be in get ready to fire loading and work the bolt firing with rest : in order that the shooting may be uniform the piece should always be rest at the same point section 11 the course in small-arm firing the course in small-arm firing consist of -- -lrb- a -rrb- nomenclature and care of rifle -lrb- b -rrb- sighting drill -lrb- c -rrb- position and aim drill -lrb- d -rrb- deflection and elevation correction drill -lrb- e -rrb- gallery practice -lrb- f -rrb- estimate distance drill -lrb- g -rrb- individual known-distance firing instruction practice -lrb- h -rrb- individual known-distance firing record practice -lrb- i -rrb- long-distance practice -lrb- j -rrb- practice with telescopic sight -lrb- k -rrb- instruction combat practice -lrb- l -rrb- combat practice -lrb- m -rrb- proficiency test the regulation govern these be find in small arm firing manual 1913 there should be several copy of this manual in every company section 12 target the accompany plate show the detail and size of the target : -lrb- illustration : target a -rrb- -lrb- regulation the word pistol appear the regulation apply with equal force to the revolver if applicable to that weapon -rrb- 135 -lrb- 9 -rrb- nomenclature and care of the weapon handling and precaution against accident -- the soldier will first be teach the nomenclature of those part of the weapon necessary to a understanding of its action and use and the proper measure for its care and preservation ordnance pamphlet no 1866 -lrb- description of the colt 's automatic pistol -rrb- 1919 and 1927 -lrb- description of the colt 's revolver caliber 38 and 45 respectively -rrb- contain full information on this subject and be furnish to organization arm with these weapon -lrb- footnote 9 : the number refer to paragraph in the small arm firing manual 1918 -rrb- careless handling of the pistol or revolver be the cause of many accident and result in broken part of the mechanism the follow rule will if follow prevent much trouble of this character : -lrb- a -rrb- on take the pistol from the armrack or holster take out the magazine and see that it be empty before replace it then draw back the slide and make sure that the piece be unloaded observe the same precaution after practice on the target range and again before replace the pistol in the holster or in the armrack when take the revolver from the armrack or holster and before return it to the same open the cylinder and eject empty shell and cartridge before begin a drill and upon arrive on the range observe the same precaution -lrb- b -rrb- neither load nor cock the weapon until the moment of firing nor until a run in the mount course be start -lrb- c -rrb- always keep the pistol or revolver in the position of raise pistol -lrb- par 146 cavalry drill regulation 1916 -rrb- except when it be pointed at the target -lrb- the position of lower pistol be authorize for mount firing only -rrb- -lrb- d -rrb- do not place the weapon on the ground where sand or earth can enter the bear or mechanism -lrb- e -rrb- before load the pistol draw back the slide and look through the bear to see that it be free from obstruction before load the revolver open the cylinder and look through the bear to see that it be free from obstruction when load -lrb- 10 -rrb- the pistol for target practice place five cartridge in the magazine and insert the magazine in the handle draw back the slide and insert the first cartridge in the chamber and carefully lower -lrb- 11 -rrb- the hammer fully down -lrb- footnote 10 : to load pistol : be at raise pistol -lrb- right hand grasp stock at the height of and 6 inch in front of the point of the right shoulder forefinger alongside barrel barrel to the rear and inclined forward about 30 ° -rrb- without derange position of the hand rotate the pistol so the sight move to the leave the barrel point to the right front and up with the thumb and forefinger of the left hand -lrb- thumb to the right -rrb- grasp the slide and pull it toward the body until it stop and then release it the pistol be thus load and the hammer at full cock if the pistol be to be keep in the hand and not to be fire at once engage the safety lock with the thumb of the right hand if the pistol be to be carry in the holster remove safety lock if on and lower the hammer fully down -rrb- -lrb- footnote 11 : to lower the hammer : be at the load position at full cock i firmly seat thumb of right hand on the hammer : insert forefinger inside trigger guard ii with thumb of left hand exert a momentary pressure on the grip-safety to release hammer from sear iii at the same instant exert pressure or the trigger and carefully and slowly lower the hammer fully down iv remove finger from trigger v insert pistol in holster caution -- the pistol must never be place in the holster until hammer be fully down -rrb- in load the revolver place five cartridge in the cylinder and let the hammer down on the empty chamber -lrb- f -rrb- whenever the pistol be be load or unloaded the muzzle must be keep up -lrb- g -rrb- do not point the weapon in any direction where a accidental discharge might do harm -lrb- h -rrb- after load do not cock the pistol or the revolver until ready to fire -lrb- i -rrb- keep the work part properly lubricate 136 position dismount -- stand firmly on both foot body perfectly balanced and erect and turn at such a angle as be most comfortable when the arm be extend toward the target the foot far enough apart to insure firmness and steadiness or position -lrb- about 8 to 10 inch -rrb- weight of body bear equally upon both foot right arm fully extend left arm hang naturally remark -- the right arm may be slightly bent although the difficulty of hold the pistol uniformly and of keep it as well as the forearm in the same vertical plane make this objectionable 137 the grip -- grasp the stock as high as possible with the thumb and last three finger the forefinger alongside the trigger guard the thumb extend along the stock the barrel hand and forearm should be as nearly in one line as possible when the weapon be pointed toward the target the grasp should not be so tight as to cause tremor of the hand or arm to be communicate to the weapon but should be firm enough to avoid lose the grip when the recoil take place remark -- the force of recoil of the pistol or revolver be exert in a line above the hand which grasp the stock the lower the stock be grasp the greater will be the movement or jump of the muzzle cause by the recoil this not only result in a severe strain upon the wrist but in loss of accuracy if the hand be place so that the grasp be on one side of the stock the recoil will cause a rotary movement of the weapon toward the opposite side the release of the sear cause a slight movement of the muzzle generally to the leave the position of the thumb along the stock overcome much of this movement the soldier should be encourage to practice this method of hold until it become natural to do uniform shoot the weapon must be hold with exactly the same grip for each shot not only must the hand grasp the stock at the same point for each shot but the tension of the grip must be uniform 138 -lrb- a -rrb- the trigger squeeze -- the trigger must be squeeze in the same manner as in rifle dring -lrb- see chapter viii section 6 -rrb- the pressure of the forefinger on the trigger should be steadily increase and should be straight back not sideways the pressure should continue to that point beyond which the slightest movement will release the sear then when the aim be true the additional pressure be apply and the pistol fire only by much practice can the soldier become familiar with the trigger squeeze this be essential to accurate shooting it be the most important detail to master in pistol or revolver shooting -lrb- b -rrb- self-cocking action -- the force require to squeeze the trigger of the revolver when the self-cocking device be use be considerably greater than with the single action to accustom a soldier to the use of the self-cocking mechanism and also to strengthen and develop the muscle of the hand a few minute practice daily in hold the unloaded revolver on a mark and snap it use the self-cocking mechanism be recommend the use of the self-cocking device in firing be not recommend except in emergency by practice in cock the revolver the soldier can become sufficiently expert to fire very rapidly use single action while he accuracy will be greater than when use double action 139 aim -- except when deliver rapid or quick fire the rear and front sight of the pistol be use in the same manner as the rifle sight the normal sight be habitually use -lrb- see pl vi -rrb- and the line of sight be direct upon a point just under the bull 's - eye at 6 o'clock the front sight must be see through the middle of the rear-sight notch the top be on a line with the top of the notch care must be take not to cant the pistol to either side -lrb- 12 -rrb- -lrb- footnote 12 : the instructor should take cognizance of the fact that the proper aim point be often affect by the personal and fixed peculiarity of the firer and if unable to correct such abnormality permit firer to direct sight at such point as promise effective result -rrb- if the principle of aim have not be teach the soldier 's instruction will begin with sighting drill as prescribe for the rifle so far as they may be applicable the sighting bar with open sight will be use to teach the normal sight and to demonstrate error likely to be commit to construct a sighting rest for the pistol -lrb- see pl vi -rrb- take a piece of wood about 10 inch long 1-1\/4 inch wide and 9\/16 inch thick shape one end so that it will fit snugly in the handle of the pistol when the magazine have be remove screw or nail this stick to the top of a post or other object at such a angle that the pistol when place on the stick will be approximately horizontal a suitable sighting rest for the revolver may be easily improvise -lrb- illustration : plate vi -rrb- 140 -lrb- a -rrb- how to cock the pistol -- the pistol should be cock by the thumb of the right hand and with the least possible derangement of the grip the forefinger should be clear of the trigger when cock the pistol some man have difficulty at first in cock the pistol with the right thumb this can be overcome by a little practice jerk the pistol forward while hold the thumb on the hammer will not be permit -lrb- b -rrb- how to cock the revolver -- the revolver should be cock by put the thumb on the hammer at as nearly a right angle to the hammer as possible and by the action of the thumb muscle alone bring the hammer back to the position of full cock some man with large hand be able to cock the revolver with the thumb while hold it in the position of aim or raise pistol where the soldier 's hand be small this can not be do and in this case it assist the operation to give the revolver a slight tilt to the right and upward -lrb- to the right -rrb- particular care should be take that the forefinger be clear of the trigger or the cylinder will not revolve jerk the revolver forward while hold the thumb on the hammer will not be permit 141 position and aim and aim drill dismount the man take the position describe in paragraph 136 except that the pistol be hold at raise pistol the instructor caution trigger squeeze exercise at the command ready cock the time put the forefinger inside the trigger guard and gradually feel the trigger inhale enough air to comfortably fill the lung and gradually raise the piece until the line of sight be direct at the point of aim i e just below the bull 's - eye at 6 o'clock while the sight be direct upon the mark gradually increase the pressure on the trigger until it reach that point where the slightest additional pressure will release the sear then when the aim be true the additional pressure necessary to fire the piece be give so smoothly as not to derange the alignment of the sight the weapon will be hold on the mark for a instant after the hammer fall and the soldier will observe what effect if any the squeeze of the trigger have have on he aim it be impossible to hold the arm perfectly still but each time the line of sight be direct on the point of aim a slight additional pressure be apply to the trigger until the piece be finally discharge at one of the moment when the sight be correctly align upon the mark when the soldier have become proficient in take the proper position the trigger squeeze should be execute at will the instructor preface the preparatory command by at will and give the command halt at the conclusion of the exercise when the soldier will return to the position of raise pistol at first this exercise should be execute with deliberation but gradually the soldier will be teach to catch the aim quickly and to lose no time in begin the trigger squeeze and bring it to the point where the slightest additional pressure will release the sear remark -- in service few opportunity will be offer for slow aim fire with the pistol or revolver although use will be make of the weapon under circumstance when accurate point and rapid manipulation be of vital importance in deliver a rapid fire the soldier must keep he eye fix upon the mark and after each shot begin a steadily increase pressure on the trigger try at the same time to get the sight as nearly on the mark as possible before the hammer again fall the great difficulty in quick firing with the pistol lie in the fact that when the front sight be bring upon the mark the rear sight be often find to be outside the line join the eye with the mark this tendency to hold the pistol obliquely can be overcome only by a uniform manner of hold and point this uniformity be to be attain only by acquire a grip which can be take with certainty each time the weapon be fire it be this circumstance which make the position and aim drill so important the soldier should constantly practice point the pistol until he acquire the ability to direct it on the mark in the briefest interval of time and practically without the aid of sight the soldier then repeat the exercise with the pistol in the left hand the left side be turn toward the target 142 to draw and fire quickly -- snap shooting -- with the squad form as describe in paragraph 141 except that the pistol be in the holster and the flap if any button the the target squeeze the trigger and at the instant the weapon be bring in line with the eye and the objective increase the pressure release the sear to enable the soldier to note error in point the weapon will be momentarily hold in position after the fall of the hammer effort at deliberate aim in this exercise must be discourage remark under paragraph 141 be specially applicable also to this type of fire when the soldier have become proficient in the detail of this exercise it should be repeat at will the instructor caution at will quick fire exercise the exercise should be practice until the mind the eye and trigger finger act in unison to simulate this type of fire mount the instructor place the squad so that the simulated bull 's - eye be in turn to the right to the leave to the
