give in paragraph 147 to 199 small arm firing manual 1913 chapter ix extract from manual of interior guard duty unite state army 1914 -lrb- the number refer to paragraph in the manual -rrb- section 1 introduction 1 guard may be divide into four class : exterior guard interior guard military police and provost guard 2 exterior guard be use only in time of war they belong to the domain of tactic and be treat of in the field service regulation and in the drill regulation of the different arm of the service the purpose of exterior guard be to prevent surprise to delay attack and otherwise to provide for the security of the main body on the march they take the form of advance guard rear guard and flank guard at a halt they consist of outpost 3 interior guard be use in camp or garrison to preserve order protect property and to enforce police regulation in time of war such sentinel of a interior guard as may be necessary be place close in or about a camp and normally there be a exterior guard further out consist of outpost in time of peace the interior guard be the only guard in a camp or garrison 4 military police differ somewhat from either of these class -lrb- see field service regulation -rrb- they be use in time of war to guard prisoner to arrest straggler and deserter and to maintain order and enforce police regulation in the rear of army along line of communication and in the vicinity of large camp 5 provost guard be use in the absence of military police generally in conjunction with the civil authority at or near large post or encampment to preserve order among soldier beyond the interior guard section 2 classification of interior guard 6 the various element of a interior guard classify accord to they particular purpose and the manner in which they perform they duty be as follow : -lrb- a -rrb- the main guard -lrb- b -rrb- special guard : stable guard park guard prisoner guard herd guard train guard boat guard watchmen etc section 3 detail and roster 7 at every military post and in every regiment or separate command in the field a interior guard will be detail and duly mount it will consist of such number of officer and enlist man as the commanding officer may deem necessary and will be command by the senior officer or noncommissioned officer therewith under the supervision of the officer of the day or other officer detail by the commanding officer 8 the system of sentinel on fix post be of value in discipline and training because of the direct individual responsibility which be impose and require to be discharge in a definite and precise manner while the desirability of this type of duty be recognize it should only be put in practice to a extent sufficient to insure thorough instruction in this method of perform guard duty and should not be the routine method of its performance the usual guard duty will be perform by watchman patrol or such method as in the opinion of the commanding officer may best secure result under the particular local condition 9 at post where there be less than three company the main guard and special guard may all be furnish by one company or by detail from each company it be direct that whenever possible such guard shall be furnish by a single company for the reason that if guard detail be take from each organization at a post of two company troops or battery it will result in both be so reduce as to seriously interfere with drill and instruction whereas if detail be take from only one the other be available for instruction at full strength where there be three or more company the main guard will if practicable be furnish by a single company and as far as practicable the same organization will supply all detail for that day for special guard overseer and fatigue duty in this case the officer of the day and the officer of the guard if there be any will if practicable be from the company furnish the guard 10 at a post or camp where the headquarters of more than one regiment be station or in the case of a small brigade in the field if but one guard be necessary for the whole command the detail will be make from the headquarters of the command if formal guard mount be to be hold the adjutant sergeant major and band to attend guard mount will be designate by the commanding officer 11 when a single organization furnish the guard a roster of organization will be keep by the sergeant major under the supervision of the adjutant -lrb- see appendix b -rrb- 12 when the guard be detail from several organization roster will be keep by the adjutant of officer of the day and officer of the guard by name by the sergeant major under the supervision of the adjutant of sergeant corporal musician and private of the guard by number per organization and by first sergeant of sergeant corporal musician and private by name -lrb- see appendix a -rrb- 13 when organization furnish they own stable or stable and park guard credit will be give each for the number of enlist man so furnished as though they have be detail for main guard 14 special guard other than stable or park guard will be credit the same as for main guard credit with fatigue duty carry on special duty or credit as the commanding officer may direct -lrb- par 6 221 247 and 300 -rrb- 15 captain will supervise the keep of company roster and see that all duty perform be duly credit -lrb- see par 355-364 a r for rule govern roster and form 342 a g o for instruction as to how roster should be keep -rrb- 16 there will be a officer of the day with each guard unless in the opinion of the commanding officer the guard be so small that he service be not need in this case a officer will be detail to supervise the command and instruction of the guard for such period as the commanding officer may direct 17 when more than one guard be require for a command a field officer of the day will be detail who will receive he order from the brigade or division commander as the latter may direct when necessary be detail as supernumerary officer of the guard for purpose of instruction 19 officer serve on staff department be in the discretion of the commanding officer exempt from guard duty 20 guard detail will if practicable be post or publish the day precede the beginning of the tour and officer notify personally by a write order at the same time 21 the strength of guard and the number of consecutive day for which a organization furnish the guard will be so regulate as to insure private of the main guard a interval of not less than five day between tour when this be not otherwise practicable extra and special duty man will be detail for night guard duty still perform they daily duty when so detail a roster will be keep by the adjutant show the duty perform by they 22 the member of main guard and stable and park guard will habitually be relieve every 24 hour the length of the tour of enlist man detail as special guard other than stable or park guard will be so regulate as to permit of manual all detail will be make by roster section 4 commander of the guard 41 the commander of the guard be responsible for the instruction and discipline of the guard he will see that all of its member be correctly instruct in they order and duty and that they understand and properly perform they he will visit each relief at least once while it be on post and at least one of these visit will be make between 12 o'clock midnight and daylight 42 he receive and obey the order of the commanding officer and the officer of the day and report to the latter without delay all order to the guard not receive from the officer of the day he transmit to he successor all material instruction and information relate to he duty 43 he be responsible under the officer of the day for the general safety of the post or camp as soon as the old guard march away from the guardhouse in case of emergency while both guard be at the guardhouse the senior commander of the two guard will be responsible that the proper action be take 44 officer of the guard will remain constantly with they guard except while visit patrol or necessarily engage elsewhere in the performance of they duty the commanding officer will allow a reasonable time for meal 45 a commander of a guard leave he post for any purpose will inform the next in command of he destination and probable time of return 46 except in emergency the commander of the guard may divide the night with the next in command but retain he responsibility the one on watch must be constantly on the alert 47 when any alarm be raise in camp or garrison the guard will be inform immediately -lrb- par 234 -rrb- if the case be serious the proper call will be sound and the commander of the guard will cause the commanding officer and the officer of the day to be at once notify 48 if a sentinel call : the guard the commander of the guard will at once send a patrol to the sentinel 's post if the danger be great in which case the sentinel will discharge he piece the patrol will be as strong as possible 49 when practicable there should always be a officer or noncommissioned officer and two private of the guard at the guardhouse in addition to the sentinel there on post 50 between reveille and retreat when the guard have be turn out for any person entitle to the compliment -lrb- see par 222 and 224 -rrb- the commander of the guard if a officer will receive the report of the sergeant return the salute of the latter with the right hand he will then draw he saber and place himself two pace in front of the center of the guard when the person for whom the guard have be turn out approach he face he guard and command : 1 _ present _ 2 arm face to the front and salute when he salute be acknowledge he resume the carry face about and command : 1 _ order _ 2 arm and face to the front if it be a officer entitle to inspect the guard after salute and before bring he guard to a order the officer of the guard report : sir all present or account for or sir -lrb- so-and-so -rrb- be absent or if the roll call have be omit : sir the guard be form except that at guard mount the commander of the guard present they guard and salute without make any report between retreat and reveille the commander of the guard salute and report but do not bring the guard to a present 51 to those entitle to have the guard turn out but not entitle to inspect it no report will be make nor will a report be make to any officer unless he halt in front of the guard 52 when a guard command by a noncommissioned officer be turn out as a compliment or for inspection the noncommissioned officer standing at a right shoulder on the right of the right guide command : 1 _ present _ 2 arm he then execute the rifle salute if a report be also require he will after salute and noncommissioned officer and sentinel relative to the instruction they may have receive from the old guard he will see that patrol and visit of inspection be make as direct by the officer of the day 61 important duty of a sentinel in this connection : -lrb- circular -rrb- war department adjutant general 's office _ washington_november_1_1887 _ by direction of the secretary of war the follow be publish for the information of the army : unite state circuit court eastern district of michigan August 1 1887 the united state v jame clark the circuit court have jurisdiction of a homicide commit by one soldier upon another within a military reservation of the united state if a homicide be commit by a military guard without malice and in the performance of he suppose duty as a soldier such homicide be excusable unless it be manifestly beyond the scope of he authority or be such that a man of ordinary sense and understanding would know that it be illegal it seem that the sergeant of the guard have a right to shoot a military convict if there be no other possible means of prevent he escape the common-law distinction between felony and misdemeanor have no application to military offens while the finding of a court of inquiry acquit the prisoner of all blame be not a legal bar to a prosecution it be entitle to weight as a expression of the view of the military court of the necessity of use a musket to prevent the escape of the deceased \* \* \* \* \* by order of the secretary of war : r c drum _ adjutant_general _ the follow be take from circular no 3 of 1883 from headquarters department of the columbium : vancouver barracks w t _ april_20_1883 _ to the assistant adjutant general _ department_of_the_columbia _ sir : \* \* \* \* \* a sentinel be place as guard over prisoner to prevent they escape and for this purpose he be furnish a musket with ammunition to prevent escape be he first and most important duty \* \* \* \* \* i suppose the law to be this : that a sentinel shall not use more force or violence to prevent the escape of a prisoner than be necessary to effect that object but if the prisoner after be order to halt continue he flight the sentinel may maim or even kill he and it be he duty to do so a sentinel who allow a prisoner to escape without firing upon he and firing to hit he be in my judgment guilty of a most serious military offense for which he should and would be severely punish by a general court-martial \* \* \* \* \* -lrb- sign -rrb- henry a morrow _ colonel_twenty-first_infantry_commanding_post _ -lrb- third indorsement -rrb- office judge advocate military division of the pacific _ may_11_1883 _ respectfully return to the assistant adjutant general military division of the pacific concur fully in the view express by col morrow i be not aware that such a view have ever be question that the period be a time of peace do not affect the authority and duty of the sentinel or guard to fire upon the escape prisoner if this escape can not otherwise be prevent he should of course attempt to stop the prisoner before firing by order he to halt and will properly warn he by the word halt or i fire or word to such effect w winthrop _ judge_advocate _ -lrb- fourth indorsement -rrb- headquarters military division of the pacific _ may_11_1883 _ respectfully return to the commanding general department of the columbium approve the after long march or when the guard be very small the field music may be dispense with chapter x map reading and sketch section 1 military map reading when you pick up a map the first question be where be the north this can usually be tell by a arrow -lrb- see fig 1 section 1 -rrb- which will be find in one of the corner of the map and which point to the true north -- the north of the north star on some map no arrow be to be find the chance be a hundred to one that the north be at the top of the map as it be on almost all print map but you can only assure yourself of that fact by check the map with the ground it represent for instance if you ascertain that the city of philadelphium be due east of the city of columbus then the philadelphia-columbus line on the map be a due east-and-west line and establish at once all the other map direction now the map represent the ground as nearly as it can be represent on a flat piece of paper if you be stand up face the north you right hand will be in the east you leave in the west and you back to the south it be the same with a map if you look across it in the direction of the arrow -- that be toward its north -- you right hand will be toward what be east on the map you left hand to the west the south will be at the bottom of the map there be another kind of a arrow that sometimes appear on a map it be like the one in figure 2 section 1 and point not to the true north but to the magnetic north which be the north of the compass though the compass needle and therefore the arrow that represent it on the map do not point exactly north the deviation be from a military point of view slight and appreciable error will rarely result through the use of the magnetic instead of the true north in the solution of any military problem -lrb- illustration : fig 1 fig 2 fig 3 fig 4 fig 5 -rrb- should you be curious to know the exact deviation consult you local surveyor or any civil engineer both arrow may appear on you map in that case disregard the magnetic arrow unless you be use the map in connection with a compass if a map be be use on the ground the first thing to be do be to put the line of the map parallel to the real outline of the ground form and road fence railroad etc that the map show for the making of a map be no more than the drawing on paper of line parallel to and proportional in length to real direction and distance on the ground for instance the road between two place run due north and south then on the map a line represent the road will be parallel to the arrow show the north and will be proportional in length to the real road in this way a map be a picture or better a bare outline sketch and as we can make out a picture though it be upside down or crooked on the wall so we call use a map that be upside down or not parallel to the real ground form but it be easier to make out both the picture and the map if they line be parallel to what they represent so in use a map on the ground we always put the line parallel to the actual feature they show this be easy if the map have a arrow if the map have no arrow you must locate object or feature on the ground and on the map they representation draw on the map a line connect any two of the feature place this line parallel to all imaginary line through the two actual feature located and you map will be correctly place look to it that you do not reverse on the map the position of the two object or feature or you map will be exactly upside down when the map have be turn into the proper position -- that be to say orient -- the next thing be to locate on the map you position if you be in the village of easton and there be a place on the map label easton the answer be apparent but if you be out in the country at a unlabeled point that look like any one of a dozen other similar point the task be more complicate in this latter case you must locate and identify both on the map and on the ground other point -- hill village peculiar bend in river forest -- any ground feature that have some easily recognizable peculiarity and that you can see from you position suppose for instance you be near leavenworth and want to locate you exact position of which you be uncertain you have the map show in this manual and look about you see southwest from where you stand the united state penitentiary also halfway between the south and the southeast -- south-southeast a sailor would say -- the reservoir -lrb- rectangle west of o in missourus -rrb- have orient you map draw on it a line from the map position of the reservoir toward its actual position on the ground similarly draw a line from the map position of penitentiary toward its actual position prolong the two line until they intersect the intersection of the line will mark the place where you stand -- south merritt hill this method consist merely in draw on the map line that represent the line of sight to know and visible place the line pass through the map position of the place you see and be parallel to the actual line of sight therefore they be the map representation of the line of sight and they intersection be the map position of the eye of the observer after this orientation and location of position one can deduce from the map everything there be to know in regard to direction in this respect study of the ground itself will show no more than will study of the map after what direction come how far to answer this one must understand that the map distance between any two point show bear a fixed and definite relation or proportion to the real distance between the two point for instance : we measure on a map and find the distance between two point to be 1 inch then we measure the real distance on the ground and find it to be 10000 inch hence the relation between the map distance and the real distance be 1 to 10000 or 1\/10000 now if the map be properly draw the same relation will hold good for all distance and we can obtain any ground distance by multiply by 10000 the corresponding map distance this relation need not be 1\/10000 but may be anything from 1\/100 that a architect might use in make a map or plan of a house up to one over a billion and a half which be about the proportion between map and real distance in a pocket-atlas representation of the whole world on a 6-inch page map maker call this relation the scale of the map and put it down in a corner in one of three way first 1 inch equal 100 second 1\/100 third as show in figure 3 -lrb- section 1 -rrb- these expression mean one and the same thing a variation of the first method on a map of different scale might be : 1 inch equal 1 mile since a mile contain 63360 inch then the real distance between any two point show on the map be 63360 time the map distance to find the ground distance by the third kind of scale copy it on the edge of a slip of paper apply the slip directly to the map and read off the distance and so we answer the question how far after direction and distance come the interpretation of the sign symbol and abbreviation on the map those authorize be give in section 2 -lrb- a reprint of appendix 4 field service regulation 1914 -rrb- but there be a good many other conventional sign in common use a key to they be publish by the war department and be call conventional sign unite state army from these you read at once the natural and artificial feature of the country show on you map it should be bear in mind that these conventional sign be not necessarily draw to scale as be the distance they show the position and outline of the feature rather than the size this for the reason that many of the feature show if draw to scale would be so small that one could not make they out except with a magnifying glass if the exact dimension be of any importance they will be write in figure on the map for instance bridge in addition to te above conventional sign we have contour to show the elevation depression slope and shape of the ground abroad hachure be much use but they serve only to indicate elevation and as compare to contour be of little value contour resemble the line show in figure 4 -lrb- section 1 -rrb- hachure be show in figure 5 -lrb- section 1 -rrb- and may be find on any european map they simply show slope and when carefully draw show steeper slope by heavier shading and gentler slope by the fainter hachure the crest of the mountain be within the hachure -lrb- see fig 5 section 1 -rrb- _ contour _ -- a certain student when ask by he instructor to define space say : i have it sir in my head but can not put it into word the instructor reply : i suppose that under those circumstance mr -- the definition really would not help much and so it be with contour -- the definition do not help much if you know a contour when you meet it on a map for example of contour turn to the map in section 2 and start at the united state penitentiary note the smooth flow irregular curved line marked 880 860 840 840 860 etc the only other line on the map that at all resemble contour be stream line like corral creek but the stream line be readily distinguish from contour by the fact that they cross the contour squarely while the contour run approximately parallel to each other note the stream line just to the west of south merritt hill the contour represent line on the ground that be horizontal and whose meanderings follow the surface just as the edge of a flood would follow the irregularity of the hill about it those line that contour stand for be just as level as the water 's edge of a lake but horizontally they wander back and forth to just as great a degree the line marked 880 at the penitentiary pass through on that particular piece of ground every point that be 880 foot above sea level should the missourus river rise in flood to 880 foot the penitentiary would be on a island the edge of which be mark by the 880 contour contour show several thing among they the height of the ground they cross usually the contour have label on it in figure the height above some start point call the datum plane -- generally sea level if with a survey instrument you put in on a piece of ground a lot of stake each one of which be exactly the same height above sea level -- that be run a line of level -- then make a map show the locution of the stake a line draw on the map through all the stake position be a contour and show the position of all point of that particular height on any give map all contour be equally space in a vertical direction and the map show the location of a great number of point at certain fixed level if you know the vertical interval between any two adjacent contour you know the vertical interval for all the contour on that map for these interval on a give map be all the same with reference to a point through which no contour pass we can only say that the point in question be not higher than the next contour up the hill nor lower than the next one down the hill for the purpose of any problem it be usual to assume that the ground slope evenly between the two adjacent contour and that the vertical height of the point above the lower contour be proportional to its horizontal distance from the contour as compare to the whole distance between the two contour for instance on the map find the height of point a the horizontal measurement be as show on the map the vertical distance between the contour be 20 foot a be about one-quarter of the distance between the 800 and the 820 contour and we assume its height to be one-quarter of 20 foot -lrb- 5 foot -rrb- higher than 800 foot so the height of a be 805 foot the vertical interval be usually indicate in the corner of the map by the letter v i for instance : v i = 20 foot on map of very small piece of ground the v i be usually small -- perhaps as small as 1 foot on map of large area on a small scale it may be very great -- even 1000 foot contour also show slope it have already be explain that from any contour to the next one above it the ground rise a fixed number of foot accord to the vertical interval of that map from the scale of distance on the map the horizontal distance between any two contour can be find for example : on the map the horizontal distance between d and e be 90 yard or 270 foot the vertical distance be 20 foot the v i of the map the slope then be 20\/270 = 1\/135 = 7-1\/2 % = 4-1\/2 ° in all of which different way the slope can be express -lrb- illustration -rrb- on a good many contoured map a figure like this will be find in one of the corner : -lrb- illustration -rrb- on that particular map contour separate by the distance -lrb- illustration -rrb- on the vertical scale show a slope of 1 ° : if separate by the distance -lrb- illustration -rrb- they show a 2 ° slope etc a slope of 1 ° be a rise of 1 foot in 57 to use this scale of slope copy it on the edge of a piece of paper just as you do the scale of distance and apply it directly to the map you will notice that where the contour lie closest the slope be steepest where they be farthest apart the ground be most nearly flat it have already be set forth how contours show height and slope in addition to this they show the shape of the ground or ground form each single contour show the shape at its particular level of the hill or valley it outline for instance the 880 contour about the penitentiary show that the hill at that level have a shape somewhat like a horse 's head similarly every contour on the map give we the form of the ground at its particular level and know these ground form for many level we can form a fair conception of what the whole surface be like a round contour like the letter o outline a round ground feature a long narrow one indicate a long narrow ground feature different hill and depression have different shape a good many of they have one shape at one level and another shape at another level all of which information will be give you by the contour on the map one of the way to see how contours show the shape of the ground be to pour half a bucket of water into a small depression in the ground the water 's edge will be exactly level and if the depression be approximately round the water 's edge will also be approximately round the outline will look something like figure 6 draw roughly on a piece of paper a figure of the same shape and you will have a contour show the shape of the bit of ground where you pour you water next with you heel gouge out on one edge of you little pond a small round bay the water will rush in and the water-mark on the soil will now be shape something like figure 7 alter you drawing accordingly and the new contour will show the new ground shape again do violence to the face of nature by digging with a stick a narrow inlet open out of you miniature ocean and the watermark will now look something like figure 8 alter you drawing once more and you contour show again the new ground form drop into you main pond a round clod and you will have a new watermark like figure 9 to add to you draw this new contour of the same level with the one show the limit of the depression show on the draw the round island drop in a second clod this time long and narrow the watermark will be like figure 10 and the drawing of it properly place will show another island of another shape you drawing now will look like figure 11 it show a depression approximately round off which open a round bay and a long narrow bay there be also a round elevation and a long narrow one a long narrow ridge jut out between the two bay and a short broad one across the neck of the round bay -lrb- illustration : fig 6 fig 7 fig 8 fig 9 fig 10 fig 11 -rrb- now flood you lake deeply enough to cover up the feature you have introduce the new water line about as show by the dot line in figure 11 show the oblong shape of the depression at a higher level the solid line show the shape farther down the horizontal distance between the two contour at different point show where the bank be steep and where the slope be gentler put together the information that each of these contour give you and you will see how contours show the shape of the ground on the little map you have draw you have introduce all the variety of ground form there be therefore all the contour form the contour on a ordinary map seem much more complicated but this be due only to the number of they they length and many turn before they finally close on themselves or they may close off the paper but trace each one out and it will resolve itself into one of the form show in figure 11 just as the high-tide line round the continent of north and south america run a long and tortuous course but finally close back on itself so will every contour do likewise and just as truly as every bend in that high-tide mark turn out around a promontory or in around a bay so will every bend in a contour stand for a hill or a valley point to the lowland if it be a hill and to the height if it mark a valley if the map embrace a whole continent or a island all the contour will be of closed form as in figure 11 but if it embrace only it part of the continent or island some of the contour will be chop off at the edge of the map and we have the open form of contour as we would have if figure 11 be cut into two part the closed form may indicate a hill or a basin the open form a ridge or a valley sometimes a casual glance do not indicate which take up first the contour of the open type if the map show a stream run down the inside of the contour there be no difficulty in say at once that the ground feature be a valley for instance v v v and the valley of corral creek on the map but if there be no stream line do the contour bend show a valley or a ridge first of all there be a radical difference between the bend of a contour round the head of a valley and its bend round the nose of a ridge compare on the map the valley v and the ridge r the bend of the contour round the head of the valley be much sharper than the bend of the contour round the nose of the ridge this be a general truth not only in regard to map but also in regard to ground form study any piece of open ground and note how much wider be the ridge than the valley where you find a hog back or devil 's backbone you have a exception to the rule but the exception be not frequent enough to worry over to tell whether a give point be on a ridge or in a valley start from the nearest stream show on the map and work across the map to the undetermined point keep in mind that in a real trip across the country you start from the stream go up the hill to the top of a ridge down the other side of the hill to a water-course then up a hill to the top of a ridge down again up again etc that be all travel be -- valley hill valley hill valley etc though you wander till the crack o ' doom and so you map travels must go -- valley hill valley hill -- till you run off the map or come back to the start point on the map follow the r-v line v indicate valley and r ridge or hill note first the difference in sharpness in the contour bend also how the valley contour point to the highland and the ridge contour to the lowland the contour go thus : -lrb- illustration -rrb- the stream flow down the valley and the sharp angle of the contour point always _ up _ stream note also how the junction of a stream and its tributary usually make a angle that point _ down _ stream which way do this stream run water flow down hill if you be in the bed of a stream contour represent higher ground must be to you right and to you left get the elevation of these contour generally the nearest contour to the bank of the stream will cross the stream and there will be a angle or sharp turn in the contour at this cross if the point of the angle or sharp turn be toward you you be go downstream if away from you you be go upstream if the contour be number you have only to look at the number to say where the low and where the high place be but to read a map with any speed one must be quite independent of these number in ordinary map reading look first of all for the stream line the stream be the skeleton upon which the whole map be hung then pick out the hilltop and ridge and you have a body to clothe with ail the detail that will be reveal by a close and careful study of what the map maker have record as to closed contour they may outline a depression or a hill on the map 881 or 885 might be hill or pond as far as they shape be concerned but clearly they be hill for on either side be small stream run _ away _ from they if they be pond the stream line would run _ toward _ the closed contour the rest of hill valley hill will always solve the problem when there be not enough stream line show to make evident at once whether a closed contour mark a pond or a hill look in the beginning for the stream line and valley and by contrast if for no other reason the hill and ridge at once loom up to illustrate the subject of contour to aid those who have difficulty in read contoured map the following be suggest : 1 secure modeling clay and build a mound 2 use wire and slice this mound horizontally at equal vertical interval into zone then insert vertical dowel through the mound of clay 3 remove the top zone place on paper and draw outline of the bottom edge trim you paper roughly to the outline draw indicate where the hole make by the dowel pierce the paper 4 do the above with each zone of you mound 5 place these papers in proper order on dowel similarly place to one in original mound at say 1 inch vertical interval apart a skeleton mound result 6 replace the zone of the clay mound and form the original clay mound along the side of skeleton mound 7 new force all the paper sheet down the dowel onto the bottom sheet and we have a map of clay mound with contour note -- one-inch or 2-inch plank can be make into any desire form by the use of dowel and similar procedure follow people frequently ask what should i see when i read a map and the answer be give the ground as it be this be not true any more than it be true that the word the valley of the meuse bring to you mind vine-clad hill a noble river and green field where cattle graze nor can any picture ever put into you thought what the grand canyon really be what print word or paint picture can not do a map will not a map say to you here stand a hill here be a valley this stream run so and give you a good many fact in regard to they but you do not have to see anything any more than you have to visualize liege in order to learn the fact of its geography a map set forth cold fact in a alphabet all its own but a easy alphabet and one that tell with a few curving line more than many thousand word could tell section 2 sketch noncommissioned officer and select private should be able to make simple route sketch this be particularly useful in patrolling as thereby a patrol station will have its call consist of one or two letter as washington w and each operator or signalist will also have he personal signal of one or two letter as jone jo these be once adopt will not be change without due authority 2 to lessen liability of error numeral which occur in the body of a message should be spell out 3 in receive a message the man at the telescope should call out each letter as receive and not wait for the completion of a word 4 a record of the date and time of the receipt or transmission of every message must be keep 5 the duplicate manuscript of message receive at or the original send from a station should be carefully file 6 in receive message nothing should be take for grant and nothing consider as see until it have be positively and clearly in view do not anticipate what will follow from signal already give watch the communicate station until the last signal be make and be very certain that the signal for the end of the message have be give 7 every address must contain at least two word and should be sufficient to secure delivery 8 all that the sender write for transmission after the word to be count 9 whenever more than one signature be attach to a message count all initial and name as a part of the message 10 dictionary word initial letter surname of person name of city town village state and territory or name of the canadian province will be count each as one word : _ e_g _ new york district of columbium east st loui should each be count as one word the abbreviation of the name of city town village state territory and province will be count the same as if write in full 11 abbreviation of weight and measure in common use figure decimal point bar of division and in ordinal number the affix st d nd rd and th will be each count as one word letter and group of letter when such group do not form dictionary word and be not combination of dictionary word will be count at the rate of five letter or fraction of five letter to a word when such group be make up of combination of dictionary word each dictionary word so use will be count 12 the follow be exception to paragraph 55 and be count as show : a m 1 word p m 1 word o k 1 word per cent 1 word 13 no message will be consider send until its receipt have be acknowledge by the receive station the international morse or general service code 18 the international morse code be the general service code and be prescribe for use by the army of the united state and between the army and the navy of the united state it will be use on radio system submarine cable use siphon recorder visual signaling : by flag -lrb- wig-wag -rrb- torch hand lantern or beam or searchlight -lrb- without shutter -rrb- general service code 23 for the flag use with the general service code there be three motion and one position the position be with the flag hold vertically the signalman face directly toward the station with which it be desire to communicate the first motion -lrb- the dot -rrb- be to the right of the sender and will embrace a arc of 90 ° start with the vertical and return to it and will be make in a plane at right angle to the line connect the two station the second motion -lrb- the dash -rrb- be a similar motion to the left of the sender the third motion -lrb- front -rrb- be downward directly in front of the sender and instantly return upward to the first position front be use to indicate a interval 24 the beam of the searchlight though ordinarily use with the shutter like the heliograph may be use for long-distance signaling when no shutter be suitable or available in a similar manner to the flag or torch the first position be a vertical one a movement of the beam 90 ° to the right of the sender indicate a dot a similar movement to the left indicate a dash the beam be lower vertically for front 25 to use the torch or hand lantern a foot light must be employ as a point of reference to the motion the lantern be most conveniently swing out upward to the right of the footlight for a dot to the leave for a dash and raise vertically for front note -- to call a station make the call letter until acknowledge at interval give the call or signal of the call station if the call letter of a station be unknown wave flag until acknowledge in use the searchlight without shutter throw the beam in a vertical position and move it through a arc of 180 ° in a plane at right angle to the line connect the two station until acknowledge to acknowledge a call signal acknowledgment follow by the call letter of the acknowledge station signaling with heliograph flash lantern and searchlight -lrb- with shutter -rrb- general service code 26 the first position be to turn a steady flash on the receive station the signal be make by short and long flash use a short flash for dot and a long steady flash for dash the element of a letter should be slightly longer than in sound signal 27 to call a station make its call letter until acknowledge 28 if the call letter of a station be unknown signal a until acknowledged each station will then turn on a steady flash and adjust when adjustment be satisfactory to the call station it will cut off its flash and the call station will proceed with its message 29 if the receiver see that the sender 's mirror or light need adjustment he will turn on a steady flash until answer by a steady flash when the adjustment be satisfactory the receiver will cut off he flash and the sender will resume he message -lrb- illustration : the two-arm semaphore code -rrb- -lrb- illustration : the two-arm semaphore code -rrb- 30 to break the send station for other purpose turn on a steady flash sound signal 56 sound signal make by the whistle foghorn bugle trumpet and drum may well be use in a fog mist fall snow or at night they may be use with the dot and dash code in apply the general service code to whistle foghorn bugle or trumpet one short blast indicate a dot and one long blast a dash with the drum one tap indicate a dot and two tap in rapid succession a dash although these signal can be use with a dot and dash code they should be so use in connection with a preconcerted or conventional code signaling by two-arm semaphore hand flag 43 signaling by the two-arm semaphore be the most rapid method of send spelled-out message it be however very liable to error if the motion be slur over or run together in a attempt to make speed both arm should move rapidly and simultaneously but there should be a perceptible pause at the end of each letter before make the movement for the next letter rapidity be secondary to accuracy for alphabet see page follow note -- in make the interval the flag be cross downward in front of the body -lrb- just above the knee -rrb- the double interval be the chop-chop signal make twice the triple interval be chop-chop signal make three time in call a station face it squarely and make its call if there be no immediate reply wave the flag over the head to attract attention make the call at frequent interval when the sender make end of message the receiver if message be understand extend the flag horizontally and wave they until the sender do the same when both leave they station care must be take with hand flag to hold the staff so as to form a prolongation of the arm letter code infantry 47 for use with general service code or semaphore hand flag piece close by -lrb- so much -rrb- top -lrb- numeral -rrb- -- on 3d piece open by -lrb- so much -rrb- u -- up y -lrb- letter -rrb- -- such battery station chapter xiii first aid rule the bandage and dressing contain in the first-aid packet have be so treat as to destroy any germ thereon therefore when dress a wound be careful not to touch or handle that part of the dress which be to be apply to the wound a sick or injured person should always be make to lie down on he back if practicable as this be the most comfortable position and all muscle may be relax all tight article of clothing and equipment should be loosen so as not to interfere with breathing or the circulation of the blood belt collar and the trousers at the waist should be open -lrb- illustration : fig 1 -rrb- do not let mere onlooker crowd about the patient they prevent he from get fresh air and also make he nervous and excite in case of injury the heart action be generally weak from shock and the body therefore grow somewhat cold so do not remove any more clothing than be necessary to expose the injury cut or rip the clothing but do not pull it try to disturb the patient as little as possible do not touch a wound with you finger or a handkerchief or with anything else but the first-aid dress do not wash the wound with water as you may infect it do not administer stimulant -lrb- whisky brandy wine etc -rrb- unless order to do so by a doctor while in a few case stimulant be of benefit in a great many case they do positive harm especially where there have be any bleed the heart may be consider as a pump and the artery as a rubber hose which carry the blood from the heart to every part of the body the vein be the hose which carry the blood back to the heart every wound bleed some but unless a large artery or a large vein be cut the bleeding will stop after a short while if the patient be keep quiet and the first-aid dress be bind over the wound so as to make pressure on it -lrb- illustration : fig 2 -rrb- when a large artery be cut the blood gush out in spurt every time the heart beat in this case it be necessary to stop the flow of blood by press upon the hose somewhere between the heart and the leak if the leak be in the arm or hand apply pressure as in figure 1 if the leak be in the leg apply pressure as in figure 2 if the leak be in the shoulder or armpit apply pressure as in figure 3 the reason for this be that at the place indicate the artery may be press against a bone more easily than at any other place another way of apply pressure -lrb- by means of a tourniquet -rrb- be show in figure 4 place a pad of tightly roll cloth or paper or any suitable object over the artery tie a bandage loosely about the limb and then insert you bayonet or a stick and twist up the bandage until the pressure of the pad on the artery stop the leak twist the bandage slowly and stop as soon as the blood cease to flow in order not to bruise the flesh or muscle unnecessarily -lrb- illustration : fig 3 -rrb- a tourniquet may cause pain and swell of the limb and it leave on too long may cause the limb to die therefore about every half hour or so loosen the bandage very carefully but if the bleeding continue pressure must be apply again in this case apply the pressure with the thumb for five or ten minute as this cut off only the main artery and leave some of the smaller artery and the vein free to restore some of the circulation when a tourniquet be painful it be too tight and should be carefully loosen a little it the leg or arm be hold upright this also help to reduce the bleeding in these part because the heart then have to pump the blood uphill a broken bone be call a fracture the great danger in the case of a fracture be that the sharp jagged edge of the bone may stick through the flesh and skin or tear and bruise the artery vein and muscle if the skin be not break a fracture be not so serious as no germ can get in therefore never move a person with a broken bone until the fracture have be so fix that the broken end of the bone can not move -lrb- illustration : fig 4 -- improvise tourniquet -rrb- if the leg or arm be break straighten the limb gently and if necessary pull upon the end firmly to get the bone in place then bind the limb firmly to a splint to hold it in place a splint may be make of any straight stiff material -- a shingle or piece of board a bayonet a rifle a straight branch of a tree etc whatever material you use must be well pad on the side next to the limb be careful never to place the bandage over the fracture but always above and below -lrb- fig 5 6 7 8 -rrb- many surgeon think that the method of bind a broken leg to the well one and of bind the arm to the body be the best plan in the field as be the quickest and one that serve the immediate purpose -lrb- illustration : fig 5 -rrb- -lrb- illustration : fig 6 -rrb- with wound about the body the chest and abdomen you must not meddle except to protect they when possible without much handling with the material of the packet fainting shock heat exhaustion the symptom of faint shock and heat exhaustion be very similar the face be pale the skin cool and moist the pulse be weak and generally the patient be unconscious keep the patient quiet rest on he back with he head low loosen the clothing but keep the patient warm and give stimulant -lrb- whisky hot coffee tea etc -rrb- sunstroke in the case of sunstroke the face be flush the skin be dry and very hot and the pulse be full and strong in this case place the patient in a cool spot remove the clothing and make every effort to lessen the heat in the body by cold application to the head and surface generally do not under any circumstance give any stimulant or hot drink -lrb- illustration : fig 7 -rrb- -lrb- illustration : fig 8 -rrb- freezing and frostbite the part frozen which look white or bluish white and be cold should be very slowly raise in temperature by brisk but careful rubbing in a cool place and never near a fire stimulant be to be give cautiously when the patient can swallow and follow by small amount of warm liquid nourishment the object be to restore the circulation of the blood and the natural warmth gradually and not violently care and patience be necessary to do this resusitation of the apparently drown in the instruction of the army in first aid the method of resuscitation of the apparently drown as describe by schaefer will be teach instead of the sylvester method heretofore use the schaefer method of artificial respiration be also applicable in case of electric shock asphyxiation by gas and of the failure of respiration follow concussion of the brain be under water for four of five minute be generally fatal but a effort to revive the apparently drown should always be make unless it be know that the body have be under water for a very long time the attempt to revive the patient should not be delay for the purpose of remove he clothes or place he in the ambulance begin the procedure as soon as he be out of the water on the shore or in the boat the first and most important thing be to start artificial respiration without delay the schaefer method be prefer because it can be carry out by one person without assistance and because its procedure be not exhaust to the operator thus permit he if require to continue it for one or two hour when it be know that a person have be under water for but a few minute continue the artificial respiration for at least one and a half to two hour before consider the case hopeless once the patient have begin to breathe watch carefully to see that he do not stop again should the breathing be very faint or should he stop breathe assist he again with artificial respiration after he start breathing do not lift he nor permit he to stand until the breathing have become full and regular as soon as the patient be remove from the water turn he face to the ground clasp you hand under he waist and raise the body so any water may drain out of the air passage while the head remain low -lrb- figure 9 -rrb- -lrb- illustration : fig 9 -- schaefer method of artificial respiration inspiration -rrb- -lrb- illustration : fig 10 -- schaefer method of artificial respiration expiration -rrb- the patient be lay on he stomach arm extend from he body beyond he head face turn to one side so that the mouth and nose do not touch the ground this position cause the tongue to fall forward of its own weight and so prevent its fall back into the air passage turn the head to one side prevent the face come into contact with mud or water during the operation this position also facilitate the removal from the mouth of foreign body such as tobacco chew gum false tooth etc and favor the expulsion of mucus blood vomitus serum or any liquid that may be in the air passage the operator kneel straddle one or both of the patient 's thigh and face he head locate the lowest rib the operator with he thumb nearly parallel to he finger place he hand so that the little finger curl over the twelfth rib if the hand be on the pelvic bone the object of the work be defeat hence the bone of the pelvis be first located in order to avoid they the hand must be free from the pelvis and rest on the lowest rib by operate on the bare back it be easier to locate the lower rib and avoid the pelvis the nearer the end of the rib the hand be place without slide off the better the hand be thus remove from the spine the finger be nearly out of sight the finger help some but the chief pressure be exert by the heel -lrb- thenar and hypothenar eminence -rrb- of the hand with the weight come straight from the shoulder it be a waste of energy to bend the arm at the elbow and shove in from the side because the muscle of the back be stronger than the muscle of the arm the operator 's arm be hold straight and he weight be bring from he shoulder by bring he body and shoulder forward this weight be gradually increase until at the end of the three seconds of vertical pressure upon the lower rib of the patient the force be feel to be heavy enough to compress the part then the weight be suddenly remove if there be danger of not return the hand to the right position again they can remain lightly in place but it be usually better to remove the hand entirely if the operator be light and the patient a overweight adult he can utilize over 80 per cent of he weight by raise he knee from the ground and support himself entirely on he toe and the heel of he hand the latter properly place on the end of the float rib of the patient in this manner he can work as effectively as a heavy man a light feather or a piece of absorbent cotton draw out thin and hold near the nose by some one will indicate by its movement whether or not there be a current of air go and come with each force expiration and spontaneous inspiration the natural rate of breathing be 12 to 15 time per minute the rate of operation should not exceed this the lung must be thoroughly empty by three seconds of pressure then refill take care of itself pressure and release of pressure -- one complete respiration -- occupy about five seconds if the operator be alone he can be guide in each act by he own deep regular respiration or by count or by he watch lie by he side if comrade be present he can be advise by they the duration of the effort as artificial respiration should ordinarily exceed a hour indefinitely longer if there be any evidence of return animation by way of breathing speaking or movement there be liable to be evidence of life within 25 minute in patient who will recover from electric shock but where there be doubt the patient should be give the benefit of the doubt in drown especially recovery be on record after two hour or more of unconsciousness hence the schaefer method be easy of operation be more likely to be persist in aromatic spirit of ammonia may be pour on a handkerchief and hold continuously within 3 inch of the face and nose if other ammonia preparation be use they should be dilute or hold farther away try it on you own nose first when the operator be a heavy man it be necessary to caution he not to bring force too violently upon the rib as one of they might be break do not attempt to give liquid of any kind to the patient while unconscious apply warm blanket and hot-water bottle as soon as they can be obtain chapter xiv law and regulation section 1 general provision the army of the united state be govern by certain law call the article of war and certain regulation call army regulation the following list include the offens most often commit by soldier generally through ignorance or carelessness rather than viciousness violation of any rule or regulation should be carefully guard camp 13 fall to salute properly 14 disrespect or affront to a sentinel 15 abuse or neglect of he horse the basic principle of the combat tactic of the different arm be set forth in the drill
